Page 23

1934.01.17

The 19th Route Army Will Return. Dai Ji Will Consolidate the Main Force and Concentrate It in Quanzhou, with Xinghua as the Front Line. Zhang Yan Passed Through Quanzhou and Arrived in Zhangzhou. British and American Warships Landed Troops.

(Xiamen) Postal service between Zhangzhou and Xiamen resumed on the 16th, while transportation between Zhangzhou and Quanzhou was cut off. Zhang Yan arrived in Zhangzhou on the afternoon of the 16th via Quanzhou. His troops are taking the route through Quanyong to return to Zhangzhou. After the 19th Route Army retreated south, three regiments originally stationed in the Quanzhou area were transferred to Zhangzhou to assist in defense. Currently known deployments are: one regiment and two artillery battalions stationed in Zhangzhou, one battalion in Songyu, one battalion in Jimei, one battalion in Shima and Haicheng, one battalion in Qingyang between Quanzhou and Zhangzhou, one battalion in Anhai, one battalion in Dongshi, and one battalion in Shitou. All artillery shells have been transported to Zhangzhou. The Quanzhou area is the main concentration point, with Xinghua as the front line. Regarding the aftermath, Cai Tingkai is inevitably going to leave. There is no more suitable candidate than Dai Ji to handle the consolidation, because the most essential unit in the 19th Route Army was the Mao Weisou unit, known for its strict combat effectiveness and discipline, surpassing other armies. Mao's unit consisted of Dai's former subordinates. Zhang Yan's unit was second in strength, and although Zhang was close to Cai, most of his troops were also Dai's former subordinates. Neither of these two units suffered losses. With these two units as the core, Dai can effectively command the entire army. However, Dai's arrival will likely occur after the national government cancels Cai's resignation. Furthermore, Dai has not been in contact with Guangdong while in Hong Kong. The Guangdong faction sent Chen Wei Yuan to Fujian. Although Chen is an old member of the 19th Route Army, his reputation is insufficient. With Dai's arrival, the 19th Route Army will still be under the central government. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Armies in Southern Fujian Jointly Attack Zhangzhou

(Shantou) Yang Fengnian, commander of the anti-rebel forces in southern Fujian, went to the Quanzhou area on the 14th to command his troops to intercept the retreating Fujian army. Zhang Shiyu led Shen Donghai, Lin Weiran, and their respective units, setting out from Zhangpu. Ye Dingguo and Chen Linrong, with their respective detachments, set out from Longyan, Hua'an, and Zhangtai, to jointly attack Zhangzhou. Contact is expected soon. It is reported that most of the troops stationed in the Zhangzhou area are former subordinates of Zhang Zhen. Cao is in contact with Zhang Shiyu to surrender and prepare to respond. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) Jin Zhaorong, director of the rear office of the anti-rebel militia command in Fujian, and advisor Zhang Naigong, arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai on the 16th, intending to meet with Chen Yi to report on the latest situation of the Fujian militia and express their welcome. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

British and American Warships Have Both Dispatched Troops to Land

(Fuzhou) The city is currently peaceful. The British cruiser HMS Berwick dispatched half a company of troops ashore this morning to provide security. Japan has increased its landing troops. The Hai Ning steamer arrived in Hong Kong yesterday. Although it carried many minor officials of the Fujian government, there was no sign of Chen Youren. (Reuters dispatch on the 16th)

(Fuzhou) Due to the unstable situation in Fuzhou and the presence of several thousand rebel troops stationed in Nantai, the British warship HMS Berwick has dispatched forty soldiers, and the American warship USS Tulsa has dispatched twenty soldiers ashore. The number of Japanese troops landed is unknown. These guards are sufficient to protect foreigners in Fuzhou. The American missionaries on the south coast of Fuzhou were ordered by American authorities several days ago to move to safe zones to prevent the rebel army from retreating south. (Reuters dispatch on the 16th)

●Manila The US Naval Staff announced today that the US warship USS Tulsa has only dispatched thirty soldiers to land in Fuzhou to protect the lives and property of American citizens. They plan to withdraw after a stable local government is established. USS Tulsa sailed to Fuzhou the day before yesterday. Other ships have been ordered to proceed to Fujian. (National Telegraph on the 16th)

The 19th Route Army's Retreat

(Fuzhou) After Cai Tingkai flew to the provincial capital from Quanzhou on the morning of the 14th, he convened a meeting of military officers in the provincial capital. Subsequently, he issued a proclamation stating that the troop deployment to cross the river was a strategic matter, and that the main battle had not yet begun. The army should still strive to maintain the safety of Fuzhou. Another report stated that Sa Zhenbing met with Cai on the afternoon of the 14th, guaranteeing the safe passage of the 19th Route Army across the river, and ordering the Chamber of Commerce to pay the outstanding loan of 200,000 yuan and hire ships for standby, requiring the entire army to withdraw from Fuzhou within three days. On the morning of the 15th, troops here were still moving along the Fu-Xia highway. Yesterday's report that Japanese sailors had gone to Mawei to board Japanese warships was inaccurate. It is heard that the Japanese consul is still requesting his country to send more warships to Fujian to protect its nationals. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

(Fuzhou) Cai Tingkai was still stationed here yesterday afternoon, but today he left on horseback with forty cavalry soldiers, heading south towards Guangdong. Before his departure, he still issued a proclamation stating that he intended to defend the city to the death, but this was merely a facade to cover his retreat. Shortly afterwards, he asked Sa Zhenbing to take over the administrative affairs of Fuzhou during the transition period. Subsequently, the main force of the 19th Route Army also retreated south in order. Yesterday, the rebel troops in Nantai attempted to reach the mainland, but were deterred by the might of the central government. These troops, numbering about several thousand, are now staying in Nantai. Yesterday, a fire broke out in a certain battalion due to carelessness, spreading to a certain village where bombs were stored, causing a great uproar. After negotiations, they were allowed to continue their retreat. Two thousand government troops have advanced to the mouth of the Min River, and their main force is only ten miles from Fuzhou. The sound of gunfire can be clearly heard there. (Reuters dispatch on the 16th)

Warships Jiang Yuan and Others Arrive in Fuzhou

(Fuzhou) At dawn on the 16th, the navy dispatched warships Jiang Yuan and others to arrive in the provincial capital. Naval troops landed fully armed, and the sound of gunfire erupted. The rebel enemies fled completely. At eight o'clock, order was restored, and the entire city once again saw the flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun. Chen Jiliang, commander of the First Fleet, issued a proclamation upon entering Fuzhou, taking responsibility for the security of the city. Minister Chen of the Naval Department also issued a proclamation from Ninghai to reassure the people. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

Military Commission Commends Chen Shaokuan

(Nanjing) The Military Commission telegraphed on the 16th to commend Chen Shaokuan, stating that the army's recapture of Fujian was brave and loyal, and highly commendable. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Chen Yi Will Go to Fujian Within the Week. The Provincial Capital Will Still Be in Fuzhou

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held a routine meeting on the morning of the 16th, which did not discuss the appointment of the Fujian provincial government. It merely submitted the list of former provincial government committee members and department heads to the newly appointed chairman, Chen Yi, and identified the individuals with proven evidence of rebellion. The appointment of new committee members and department heads will depend on Chen Yi's proposal. According to the old provincial committee: Jiang Guangnai (Chairman), Dai Ji (Director of Civil Affairs Department), Xu Xiqing (Director of Finance Department), Zheng Zhenwen (Director of Education Department), Sun Xiwen (Director of Construction Department), Li Zhangda (Secretary-General), Gao Dengting, Lin Zhiyuan, Li Qingquan (Committee Members). Chen Yi is scheduled to depart for Fujian to assume his new post within the week. The original order was to temporarily establish the provincial capital in Yanping. According to Chu Minyi, now that the provincial capital has been recovered, it should still be located in Fuzhou. Chen will travel to Fujian by sea. According to sources in the military, after Chen goes to Fujian, he intends to first recall Cao Haosen from Beijing to preside over departmental affairs. He Yingqin has repeatedly telegraphed Cao Haosen, urging him to come to Beijing. The military has also telegraphed, urging his journey. Cao replied that he would come to Beijing after handing over the affairs of the Five Provinces Headquarters. The vacant position of Chief of Staff left by Cao is determined to be succeeded by Qian Dajun. The position of Second-in-command of the Military Affairs Department left by Chen Yi is being discussed by He Yingqin with Jiang and Wang. The Executive Yuan meeting next week will make a decision. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice and Administration believes that since Fuzhou has been recovered, personnel of all levels of courts in the province should quickly resume their duties. It has telegraphed to Wei Datong, president of the Fujian High Court, who is staying in Beiping, urging him to go south immediately, along with personnel who left their posts due to the Fujian Incident, and accompany the newly appointed chairman, Chen Yi, to Fujian to return to their posts. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Deng Longguang's Division Was Ordered to Depart for Fujian to Take Over the Defense of Pinghe and Zhao'an, Responsible for Reorganizing Dispersed Soldiers. The 14th Group Army in Southern Jiangxi Deployed Additional Defense on the Guangdong-Fujian Border.

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang decided to transfer Deng Longguang's division, stationed in Huiyang, to Fujian to take over the defense of Pinghe and Zhao'an, and be responsible for reorganizing scattered soldiers. Huang Renhuan's division was also transferred from Jiaoling back to southern Fujian to defend Shanghang and Wuping. Deng's division is scheduled to depart from Huiyang on the 17th. Chen Jitang sent several officials, including Chen Mingjing, to Fujian to assist in reorganizing the scattered soldiers. He also appointed Chen Weiyuan, a Fujian native, as the commander of the Southern Fujian Garrison. The 14th Group Army in southern Jiangxi was mobilized on the 15th to deploy additional defense on the Guangdong-Fujian border. The vanguard, Li Zhenliang's division, has already reached Dabu and is continuing to advance towards the Fujian border. Chen Zhang, Wang Zanbin, Zhang Da, and other units will subsequently arrive at the Fujian border. Li Zhenliang went from Xingning to Dabu on the 16th to command. Chen Zhang and Wang Zanbin are expected to arrive in the provincial capital on the 17th to report on defense matters. In addition, Chen Jitang ordered Li Yangjing to deploy the four divisions of Huang Renhuan, Huang Yanzhen, Huang Qiweng, and Deng Longguang to defend the seven counties on the Guangdong-Fujian border: Yongding, Shanghang, Wuping, Zhao'an, Pinghe, Raoping, and Dabu. Li Zhenliang and Zhang Ruigui's two divisions are reserved as reserves, stationed in the Meixian, Jiaoling, Fengshun, and Chaoshan areas. Southern Jiangxi is still the responsibility of Yu Hanmou's unit. (Dispatch on the 16th)

(Guangzhou) According to Zou Lu's statement to guests today, the overall situation in Fujian still contains serious possibilities. According to official sources, the Guangdong army has entered southern Fujian. According to a telegram from Li Yangjing, the Red Army on the Guangdong-Guangxi-Fujian border is now surrendering to the Guangdong army. (Reuters dispatch on the 16th)

Cui Guangxiu Departs From Guangdong for Beijing to Attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee. Chen Ce and Zhang Huichang Are Traveling With Him, As Well As Li Qian, and Huang Xuchu Is Also Departing From Nanning.

(Hong Kong) Guangdong Committee member Cui Guangxiu departed for Beijing on the Empress of Canada at 4 PM on the 16th to attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee. Chen Ce and Zhang Huichang are traveling with him. Cui said that the Political Council designated Yu to attend the Fourth Plenary Session along with Li Qian, Deng Qingyang, and Guan Su. Li and others are heading north immediately. Yu will wait for Li and others in Shanghai to enter Beijing together. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Hong Kong) Guangxi Committee member Huang Xuchu left Nanning on the 16th and is expected to arrive in Hong Kong on the 18th. He will take the President Cleveland northward on the 19th to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Guangzhou) The Guangdong province has only sent one Central Executive Committee member to attend the Fourth Plenary Session, who departed for Beijing today, carrying several important proposals from southwestern leaders. The Guangxi province has also only sent one representative to attend, who has already departed for Guangdong. It is likely that these two individuals will be the representatives of the southwestern provinces. (Reuters dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) The Central Executive Committee Secretariat has designated the Overseas Chinese Reception Center as the reception center for the Fourth Plenary Session to accommodate Central Committee members coming to Beijing from various regions. Fearing that it would not be able to accommodate everyone, the Central Hotel has been designated as the second reception center. The Liaison Section of the Central Secretariat has reserved rooms and is arranging them. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Jinan) Zhu Jiqing passed through Jinan to go to Beijing to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) The Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee telegraphed Wu Tiecheng on the 16th, stating, "Committee Member Wu Tiecheng of Shanghai: The Fourth Plenary Session is about to be held. Please inform us in advance when committee members pass through Shanghai on their way to Beijing so that we can arrange for their reception." (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Hong Kong) The committee members from Guangdong attending the Fourth Plenary Session arrived in Hong Kong by train on the evening of the 16th and immediately boarded the President Wilson to head north. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Hong Kong) Lin Yizhong and Cui Guangxiu arrived in Hong Kong by car from the provincial capital on the morning of the 13th. Cui immediately boarded the President Wilson that evening to head north to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. Lin is handling private matters and will return to the provincial capital within a few days. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Hong Kong) Chen Ce, Zhang Huichang, and Li Fulin boarded the Empress of Canada at 4 PM on the afternoon of the 16th to head north. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Hong Kong) Miss Hu Mulan arrived in the provincial capital on the evening of the 15th and returned to Hong Kong at noon on the 16th, immediately boarding a ship northward to Shanghai to transfer to Beijing to visit the Central Committee members. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Hankou) Xia Douyin is scheduled to take the Jiang Shun to Beijing on the 17th to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Li Zongren and Wang Jialie Met in Nanzhai

Negotiations on Guizhou and Guangxi Issues Were Successful

(Hong Kong) Wang Jialie and Li Zongren arrived together in Nanzhai on the border between Guizhou and Guangxi on the 10th, and successfully negotiated on Guizhou and Guangxi military, economic, and transportation matters. They returned to Guiyang and Nanning on the 12th. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Liu Guitang's Remnants Are Being Intercepted by Various Armies

Liu Fled from Quzhou to Neihuang

Bai Fengxiang Pursued Towards Handan

(Beiping) He Zhuguo telegraphed to Ping that since the bandit Liu fled south, passing through areas of devastation, he was split into two sections on the 13th in the vicinity of Sanbu Township by the cavalry division of Bai Fengxiang. One section fled towards Gucheng, while the other fled along the south of the Qingyang River, reaching the vicinity of Youfang. Wang Qifeng's division and Xu regiment happened to advance from Nangong to Yin Lutou in Qinghe County and encountered the bandits, resulting in a fierce battle lasting about three hours. Liu's regiment of Wang's division also rushed from Zaoqiang to join the Xu regiment, and together they fiercely suppressed the bandits. The bandit forces were overwhelmed and fled in a disarray. Liu Guitang led his main force to flee first towards Juntun in the west of Wucheng County. After being intercepted by the Shandong army, they returned to Wangjiazhuang within the boundary of Nanying Palace. It happened that the Xu regiment had retreated to Xie Lu Township in Qinghe County, and they encountered each other again, resulting in a fierce battle. As a result, fifty to sixty bandits were killed, and over ten bandits were captured, along with many guns, horses, and camels. The bandits fled in a hurried towards Shuiji south of Qinghe. Wang's division and Xu's two regiments are still ordered to follow and pursue. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Jinan) Liu Guitang's unit was attacked once on the 14th in Xia Bao, five miles west of Linqing, and again on the 15th in Matou, Qiu County. The bandits suffered heavy losses, and six or seven people were captured. According to their confession, Liu's unit was divided into several groups when passing through Pingyi, and they are now reunited, with over two thousand horses, two thousand guns, and about three thousand people, including ticket holders. Today, Liu's unit has fled from Quzhou to Neihuang. The Shandong army was stationed in Quzhou yesterday and is now pursuing westward, with a total of four regiments. He Zhuguo's unit is heading to Daming, and Liu Zhi has sent Gao Guizi's unit to northern Henan to join forces with the local Shandong army to encircle and suppress them. Liu's unit has been fleeing for days and is very tired. There are many deserters along the way, and several more people have been captured today. Li Hanzhang is supervising the suppression in Linqing. Zhan Shutang is now leading his unit to Fan County and is expected to arrive in Puyang on the 27th. According to a telegram from Henan, Liu's unit has only a little over a thousand people left. Sun Tonggang took the opportunity to scout Liu's unit yesterday and returned to Jinan today. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) Liu's bandit unit of over two thousand people has fled from Quzhou into Handan County. Yu Xuezhong specially telegraphed Bai Fengxiang's division to turn towards Handan to pursue, and ordered Wang Qifeng's division in Gaoyi to mobilize and suppress. After Liu's bandit unit fled to southern Hebei, a south-bound train on the Ping-Han Railway stopped in Shunde yesterday while Liu's bandits were moving away from the railway line, the train continued southward. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Yan Xishan Prepares to Mediate the Sun-Ma Conflict. Both Sides Report the Truth to Yan by Telegram. He Yingqin Sent Hou Cheng to Taiyuan to Visit Yan. The Two Armies Are Still in Contact in Shizuzi. The Military Commission Has Telegraphed Strict Orders to Stop.

(Taiyuan) Ma Hongkui sent a representative, Kang Yushu, to visit Yan in Taiyuan to negotiate on persuading Sun to stop advancing and report on the recent situation in Ningxia and Qinghai. He Yingqin's representative, Hou Cheng, is expected to arrive in Taiyuan from Beiping tomorrow. It is heard that Yan intends to mediate the Sun-Ma conflict, and both sides have sent telegrams to Yan to report the truth. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Ningxia states that the Sun and Ma units are still facing each other in Shizuzi. It is rumored that Yan of Shanxi will mediate, and the situation is not expected to escalate. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Lanzhou states that Hu Zongnan's unit has advanced to Guyuan to guard the Gansu-Ningxia border. Hu is still in Lanzhou and will not enter Ningxia until ordered. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) The Sun and Ma units are currently gathering their main forces, and it is expected that a major battle will occur within a few days. Ma Hongkui sent an urgent telegram to Bai Jianmin, his representative stationed in Beiping, reporting that Hal Yu, the director of the army's office in Baotou, was missing. He ordered him to send someone to Baotou to investigate immediately. The cavalry brigade of the 5th Joint Defense of the 2nd Division of the Sun Army in Baotou, commanded by Lu Fengnian, has fully deployed on the 15th, leaving only a small number of troops to guard. The defense of Baotou has been taken over by Wang Jingguo's division. He replied in a telegram to Ma, stating that if Sun resists the order and does not comply, he can only telegraph the Central Government to clearly order suppression. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) The Military Commission telegraphed Sun and Ma on the 16th, ordering them to cease military action and await the Central Government's disposition. It also telegraphed He Yingqin, Chairman of the Beiping Military Branch, to handle the matter successively to prevent the situation from escalating. At the same time, it also summoned the representatives of Sun and Ma stationed in Beijing, requesting each to telegraph and mediate to resolve the issue peacefully. It is heard that the Central Government is planning to relocate the Sun army to another location. Sun and Ma have both telegraphed the Central Government to request instructions on everything. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) Tomorrow, the Standing Committee of the Military Branch will put forward a method of discussing how to resolve Sun-Ma military clashes. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) The Sun and Ma units are still in contact in the Shizuzi area. Ma telegraphed He yesterday to report the situation of the Sun army's attack. He replied that he had telegraphed Sun, strictly ordering him to stop advancing to prevent the situation from escalating. The aftermath will be resolved by awaiting the Central Government's orders. If there is resistance and disobedience, he will plan other methods of handling it. Hou Cheng took He's handwritten letter this morning to visit Yan in Taiyuan. The content included asking Yan to persuade Sun to postpone his westward advance and asking Yan whether he had agreed to Sun's partial defense of Woye, and whether it was necessary to pass through Dengkou Shizuzi. Hou planned to stay in Taiyuan for one or two days before returning to Beiping to report. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) He Yingqin replied to reporters in writing, stating: 1. Before the truth of the Sun and Ma military conflict is clear, the handling methods cannot be reported. 2. The situation of the conflict between the two armies is as reported. 3. He himself will not go to Beijing for the Fourth Plenary Session. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

The Situation in Eastern Chahar Becomes Grim as Japanese and Puppet Troops Attack Longmensuo. Zhang Renjie's Unit Resists with All Efforts. Qin Dechun Visited He and Huang to Report.

(Beiping) After receiving a telegram from the Chahar Provincial Government stating that Japanese and puppet troops had attacked Longmensuo, Qin Dechun visited the two committee chairmen, He and Huang, at 4 PM to report, requesting negotiations with the Japanese. Song Zheyuan has decided to come to Beiping tomorrow. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Zhangjiakou on the evening of the 16th states that there are about several hundred Japanese troops in Zhao Jiaying outside Longmensuo, who are currently attacking the Great Wall line. Fighting has not stopped as of now. Song's brigade is strictly guarding Longmensuo. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Zhangjiakou on the 16th states that over a thousand Japanese and puppet troops suddenly launched an attack on Zhao Jiayingzi near Longmensuo on the morning of the 16th. The garrison unit led by Zhang Renjie resisted with all efforts. In the afternoon, puppet troops invaded the area and advanced towards Longmensuo. As of 5 PM, fighting was still ongoing. Zhang Renjie reported to the Chahar Provincial Government at noon that the situation in Longmensuo was critical. The Provincial Government telegraphed Tianjin and Beiping to report to Song Zheyuan and Qin Dechun, requesting instructions on how to respond. The issue in Eastern Chahar is extremely serious. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Zhangjiakou on the evening of the 16th states that two Japanese reconnaissance planes reconnoitered the area around Longmensuo and Chicheng at 11:30 AM today, but did not drop any bombs. They then flew east. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Negotiations on Receiving Gubeikou Are Making Definite Progress

(Beiping) After Yin Rugeng negotiated with the Japanese on the issue of receiving Gubeikou, definite progress has been made. Yin telegraphed his Beiping resident director, He Xiaoyi, yesterday to go to Tianjin to be given confidential instructions in person. He returned to Beiping this afternoon and went to Ju Ren Hall to visit He and report on everything. He Xiaoyi said that the issue of receiving Gubeikou can be received at any time after our side has fully prepared the receiving procedures. A commissioner's office will be established in Gubeikou, with Huo Shi internally designated as the director. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Wartime Public Bond Collateral Has Been Paid Out Yesterday

(Tianjin) Two million yuan was borrowed using wartime public bonds, with 250,000 yuan from the Central Bank and the rest borrowed from 22 banks, including the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Salt Bank. It was remitted to Beiping on the 16th to be handed over to the Wartime Relief Committee for emergency relief. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Tianjin) Wartime relief has been delayed due to lack of funds. It must be carried out after the severe cold weather. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Ma Zhongying Is Willing to Give Up Turpan

(Beiping) A telegram from Dihua states that Ma Zhongying has expressed to the provincial government his willingness to give up Turpan and requests the provincial army to take over the defense of southern Xinjiang. Military operations are expected to end. (Special dispatch on the 16th)

A Conflict Between Workers and Police at the Kailuan Coal Mines Results in a Strike. Work Was Suspended Two Days Each Week. Workers Demanded the Cancellation of the Order. Discord Led to Shooting. One Person Was Killed, and Many Were Injured. Majiagou Is Under Special Martial Law. Workers' Representatives Went to Beiping to Petition.

(Tianjin) An urgent telegram from Majiagou states that since the incident, the Kailuan Mining Bureau has suffered significant losses due to the disruption of sales routes outside the pass. Therefore, it has been stipulated that work will be suspended for two days each week at the five mines in Tongshan, Linxi, Majiagou, Zhao Fen Village, and Tongzhuangzi to save costs. The workers at these five mines, fearing for their livelihoods, gathered over four thousand workers on the afternoon of the 14th and went on strike. They also sent representatives to negotiate with the Mining Bureau to cancel the suspension of work order. The Second Security Bureau of the mining area, upon receiving the news, sent team leader Jin Qiupu and Li Enyuan to lead a team to gather the striking workers and persuade them. Discord led to violence, and one team leader and one policeman were injured. One worker was killed, three were seriously injured, and five were slightly injured. Just as the fighting intensified, the security team of the war zone arrived to suppress the situation, preventing it from escalating. However, the workers still intend to appeal to all parties within the day to make a final struggle. Majiagou has now declared special martial law, and pedestrians are prohibited at night. The mining area is entirely guarded by armed security teams. Also, when the conflict between workers and police occurred, gunshots rang out, and shops, unaware of the truth, closed their doors one after another. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

(Beiping) Kailuan miners, because the mining authorities recently changed their job plans and forced employees to stop work for two days each week, and forced them to contract small packages, which they could not bear to be exploited, gathered over four thousand workers on the 14th to discuss coping measures. Sun Wenbin, the director of the mining area security team, led armed police to the scene to suppress them, causing misunderstandings on both sides. The police team opened fire, killing one worker, Niu Changfu, and injuring more than ten people. The miners were extremely angry. On the 16th, they specially dispatched representatives, Si Zhongwu and others, to Beiping to petition the provincial party department and the Political Consolidation Committee, begging for them to uphold justice and provide assistance. The Provincial Party Department immediately telegraphed the Hebei Provincial Government to ask them to send personnel to investigate and provide condolences to the workers and properly handle the aftermath, in order to punish the murderers. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) Because of the Kailuan Coal Mine strike and the worker police clash, a labor movement was started, but the mine director Zhang Baoshi was staying in Shanghai for public business. After hearing the news, he wired all parties asking to resolve the strike, and he sent a wire to the minister Chen in the Ministry of Industry saying, to: Minister Chen, in the Ministry of Industry, concerning the Kailuan Coal Mine labor dispute, regarding the workers and police clashes, leading to disturbances, other than calling the general manager and the other managers for ways to resolve it, earnestly asking you to wire the Hebei Provincial chairman to consider the livelihood of the laborers, offer special consideration, in order to maintain the mining industry, to avoid a crisis, Baoshi, coming to Beijing today, and will return to Tianjin after asking. In addition, Baoshi also sent a wire to the Ministry of Communications (Special dispatch on the 16th)

Central Government Prepares to Organize National Defense Committee

Strengthening national defense and safeguarding territory are the inherent duties of the government. Therefore, major powers all prioritize the study of national defense. They deeply consider and meticulously plan the management of their country's naval and land fortresses, the training of combat personnel, and the preparation of wartime economy. They also pay close attention to changes in the diplomatic situation and the rise and fall of the "hypothetical enemy's" national power, all to ensure the security of their nation. Because of this, countries have a clear understanding of the strengths of both themselves and their "hypothetical enemies," leaving no room for concealment. Both sides, fearing the other's strict precautions, dare not easily start a war, thus establishing the so-called "armed peace." Our country, having no conflict with the world, is nevertheless threatened by strong neighbors. Although we do not have an explicitly designated "hypothetical enemy," we have aggressors to fear. The perilous situation is undeniable. However, internal strife and a weak national defense have prevented us from eliminating the tragedies of losing rights and suffering national humiliation.

National defense is the lifeline of a nation and requires the painstaking efforts of various specialized talents over many years to achieve a firm grasp. It cannot be accomplished overnight or through the heroic deeds of a single individual. Since the opening of our country to foreign trade, we have rarely heard of major national defense plans. Every time we suffer a major defeat, we engage in a major repentance, but it is nothing more than self-pity and regret. After a brief period of remorse, we forget everything once the situation has passed. Since the loss of the Northeast, the authorities have organized a National Defense Design Committee. However, as the name suggests, the so-called "design" is merely research. Knowing only how to research but not how to implement is no different from idle theorizing. Recently, the central government has considered forming another National Defense Committee. Does this mean that they intend to move from theoretical research to practical implementation? If so, it can be considered an important policy amidst the cries of national crisis.

Generally, when people talk about national defense, they focus on military affairs, as if there is no national defense other than military affairs. However, we believe that military affairs, finance, and diplomacy are the three pillars of national defense, interdependent and equally important. Our country maintains an army of over two million, but when enemy troops approach, we cannot drive them away because we have too many redundant soldiers and insufficient supplies. The quality cannot overcome the quantity. Today, we should either not talk about national defense or, if we do, we must first find a way to ensure that the nation's military expenditure is commensurate with its financial strength. Once soldiers are paid properly and military funds are adequately prepared, the government's credibility will naturally rise, military discipline will be easily rectified, and the improvement of combat effectiveness will inevitably accelerate. With such a strong army, dedicated to serving the country, we can then advance to fight and retreat to defend.

Furthermore, the relationship between national defense and diplomacy is also easy to understand. Su Qin persuaded the six states to form an alliance, and they listened, preventing the powerful Qin from taking advantage. The Soviet Union employed its "multilateral diplomacy" and signed non-aggression treaties with Western European countries, preventing Japanese soldiers from stepping an inch into its territory. These are all benefits of diplomacy. Conversely, the Japanese seize our territory and slaughter our people, in part because our country's diplomacy is isolated and unsupported. In the future, we hope that our authorities will have foresight and establish a diplomatic strategy that greatly benefits national defense.

In conclusion, we believe that planning national defense is urgent and must consider military affairs, finance, and diplomacy, none of which can be neglected. As the National Defense Committee is about to be established, we dare to express our sincere hope that it will fulfill its responsibilities.

Roosevelt's Message to Congress

Improve Financial Situation

Fully Control Currency

Lead to General Agreement

(Washington) President Roosevelt stated in his message to Congress: "In accordance with the progress we are now making to restore more appropriate prices, with the aim of ultimately achieving a less variable purchasing power of the dollar, I request Congress to re-authorize certain legislation to improve the financial and monetary situation. If we can make it clear that we are now establishing a permanent hard currency reserve for the government, we will be able to organize a sound and adequate currency control. Currency is a government prerogative. Many people advocate using gold and silver as the basis of our currency, either in a simple system or in a mixed ratio. Although the current world situation is chaotic, we hope that the situation can gradually lead to the formation of a general agreement in the future."

"In this time of emergency, the practice of individuals or international transfers of gold is not only unnecessary but also inappropriate. The transfer of large amounts of gold is only necessary to offset international trade balances. Therefore, it is a good policy for the ownership of gold used for currency within the country to belong to the government, and this gold should be stored in the form of gold bars rather than gold coins. The government has already issued orders to receive gold owned by private individuals or organizations. Although the Federal Reserve Bank still holds a large amount of cash, the government has the right, under current laws, to completely nationalize all monetary gold owned by the American people according to administrative law. However, because this matter is of great importance, I would rather consult with Congress and use special legislation to transfer all gold supplies owned by the American people to the government, with a clause attached to pay for the cash received with gold certificates. Gold certificates are always guaranteed by the Treasury's gold and paid in dollars according to the amount, and the weight and composition of these dollars can be specified at any time. This legislation can give the government ownership of domestic gold reserves and allow it to reduce the gold content of the dollar for the sake of public welfare, and the benefits derived therefrom also belong to the government. If there is a need to increase the gold content of the dollar for the sake of public welfare, the losses will also be borne by the government."

"Once the ownership of gold is entirely transferred to the government, all gold reserves can be a permanent fixed hard currency reserve, and its increase or decrease will only be carried out when clearing international balances or when the international agreement allocates world gold reserves in the future. Once this permanent policy is established, the time will come to more accurately determine the gold value of the dollar."

"Because the world situation is uncertain, I believe that it is not yet possible to determine the exact value for the sake of public interest. Under the current legislation, I have the right to decide that 50 percent is the permissible minimum. After careful research, I feel that redetermining the exchange rate to exceed 60 percent of the current value is not in the public interest. Therefore, I ask Congress to stipulate that redetermining the exchange rate at 60 percent is the permissible maximum. In order to prepare for greater stability in our foreign exchange rates, the Secretary of the Treasury, in addition to having the right to buy and sell gold at home and abroad, should also have the right to deal with foreign exchange, allocating 200 million yuan from the profits after the devaluation of the dollar for the purpose of buying and selling gold foreign exchange and government currency certificates, and regulating currency, maintaining credit, and other uses."

President Roosevelt hinted that current laws related to the handling of gold and other monetary matters will be amended, saying that silver has a long history as a currency standard, and it is in itself a currency. Almost half of the world's people use silver as currency, which is one of the most important parts of our own monetary structure. Silver is an element in world international commerce and should not be ignored. A notice was issued on December 21 to plan to mint silver coins, increase silver reserves, and make the United States the first country to fulfill the silver agreement. The silver agreement is a step in the right direction, and we are now fulfilling it.

President Roosevelt went on to mention the promises made at the World Economic Conference, saying that if the governments of the countries concerned fulfill these promises one by one, the use and value of silver will greatly increase. The US government can also use silver as a currency standard. I hope to increase the use of silver, but I do not want to make any recommendations to Congress at this time to expand the use of silver in currency, because I believe that we can use other monetary methods to learn more about the results of the London agreement.

President Roosevelt emphasized two principles: First, the national currency must maintain its soundness, have lasting purchasing power, and be sufficient for daily needs and the establishment of credit. Second, the government has the right to issue currency and is the sole protector and owner of the currency standard. Therefore, the government should have the right to decide the scope and nature of hard currency reserves at any time. President Roosevelt concluded by saying that he believed that the people would be able to understand the government's intention to maintain credit and establish a sound exchange medium for the needs of the people. (15th Reuters)

Roosevelt's Explanation

(Washington) President Roosevelt explained his message to Congress to reporters, saying that the most urgent goal of his monetary plan is to restore the purchasing power of the dollar to the level that prevailed when the average debt in the United States was incurred, so that debts can be repaid with dollars of the same value as when the debts were incurred. This procedure is not intended to overissue paper money. The government wants to obtain the power to allocate equalization funds for the purpose of buying government bonds, only to protect the prices of government bonds and prevent private holders of government bonds from selling them cheaply. (15th Reuters)

Roosevelt Issues Three Orders

Control Bank Private Exchange

Prevent Capital Outflow

(Washington) Today, President Roosevelt issued three orders based on his message to Congress: (1) Expanding the scope of the order of March 10 of last year, all private individuals and registered banks can engage in foreign exchange; (2) All those engaged in foreign exchange must register with the government; (3) The US Mint can receive raw gold with government permission, but the raw gold purchased must be priced according to the Treasury's regulations, with a handling fee of 35 percent. Therefore, the regulation stipulates that gold is worth 34 yuan and 43 cents per ounce. According to general observations, the second order is a step to prevent capital outflow. (15th National Telegram)

Wall Street is Enlivened

New York Designated as Free Market for Raw Gold Purchase

(New York) Since the publication of President Roosevelt's message, the atmosphere on Wall Street has been enlivened, with active trading in stocks and commodities, and government bonds are also viewed favorably. There is a rumor here that the President will designate New York as a free market for the purchase of raw gold, which can maintain international finance and investment. As for the current impact of the President's message, it has prompted a continued decline in the exchange rates of silver and gold dollars. (15th National Telegram)

Roosevelt's Monetary Policy Stabilizes Currency Prices, Concrete Steps, Extremely Positive Response in Congress

(Washington) President Roosevelt submitted the currency bill to both houses of Congress today. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau claimed that from January 16, the official price of newly mined net gold would be 34 yuan and 45 cents per ounce, minus a handling fee of 25 per thousand.

Important Provisions of New Currency

The important provisions of the currency bill are summarized as follows:

(1) Ownership of the Federal Reserve's gold reserves is transferred to the Treasury Department, and the Treasury Department gives the Reserve Bank gold certificates of equal value in US dollars.

(2) Cash must not be circulated. Gold coins are abolished. Apart from the gold certificates held by the Federal Reserve Bank, no currency may be exchanged for gold in the amount that the Secretary of the Treasury deems necessary to maintain the equal purchasing power of various currencies.

(3) The Secretary of the Treasury, with the approval of the President, has the right to buy gold at home and abroad, without limit.

(4) The Secretary of the Treasury may pay the interest on public bonds in advance and sell gold at home and abroad. In order to stabilize exchange rates, the Secretary of the Treasury may buy, sell, or discount bills of exchange, checks, and exchange notes, and receive debt instruments.

Roosevelt's Movement to Stabilize Currency Prices

The above are the main points of the currency bill. President Roosevelt said that he does not approve of paper money policies, but issuing limited, non-interest-bearing five-yuan and ten-yuan banknotes, as stipulated in the Thomas Amendment, cannot be said to be overissuing paper money. He is confident that he can stabilize the price of the dollar within a limit of 56 percent. He believes that the movement to stabilize currency prices in the United States can promote the pricing of currencies in other countries. It is estimated that the government can obtain profits from the reduction in the gold content of the dollar, amounting to between 340 million yuan and 420 million yuan.

From Tonight Onward, All Gold Will Be Nationalized

Treasury Secretary Morgenthau has set the deadline for private individuals to hand over all their gold to the Treasury Department as Wednesday night. As for the gold reserves of the Federal Reserve Bank, they are not included, estimated to be over 350 million yuan. The Financial Rehabilitation Corporation has increased its total amount to 150 million yuan, and all but 25 million yuan has been used. Domestic purchases totaled 681,000 ounces, worth 22,898,000 yuan. Foreign purchases were worth 97 million yuan. Jones, the director of the Financial Rehabilitation Corporation, claimed that the re-pricing of the dollar could enable the Rehabilitation Corporation to profit from gold, as the Rehabilitation Corporation could sell gold abroad. The Financial Rehabilitation Corporation's foreign gold is designated for withdrawal in London and Paris.

Three Executive Orders Control Foreign Exchange

President Roosevelt issued three executive orders announcing government control of foreign exchange transactions, with banks and private individuals subject to licensing policies. The White House claimed that the orders were virtually the same as the regulations issued on March 10, except that private individuals engaged in foreign exchange are also subject to the regulations, not just banks. It is said that the effect of the new orders is to allow Treasury Secretary Morgenthau to exert his influence. (15th Reuters)

Extremely Positive Response in Congress

(Washington) The impact of President Roosevelt's message on the New York market today was that the price of newly mined gold jumped from 34 yuan and 6 cents per ounce to 34 yuan and 43 cents. This number is in line with the decision to limit the gold content of the dollar to 60 percent. The initial response to President Roosevelt's message in Congress was extremely positive. Democrats unanimously supported President Roosevelt, and Senate Republicans also convened a meeting of their party to consider their policies. (15th Reuters)

Britain and France Await Final International Agreement, Dollar and Pound Both Depreciated, Franc Stable, No Problem, Japan Will Further Depress Currency Prices

(London) President Roosevelt's message to Congress arrived in London after business hours, so there was no reaction in London today. However, the public feels that the re-pricing of the dollar at 60 percent, although it affects Britain and France, is still tolerable, awaiting a final international agreement. The public expects President Roosevelt to now be willing to establish an international agreement. The United States retains the possibility of further devaluing the dollar by 11 percent. The public sees this as a tool for the United States to use for consultations with other countries. If the dollar is devalued by more than 14 percent, it will force France to abandon the gold standard, and the current advantage of the United States, which President Roosevelt wants to maintain as long as possible, will be lost. President Roosevelt's message arrived in Paris after the market closed, but both the dollar and the gold pound have depreciated today. Paris is now in a state of uncertainty and panic, but the stability of the franc seems to be no problem. (15th Havas)

(London) London did not respond with unsympathetic acceptance to the announcement of the US gold policy. The detailed explanation of this policy has reduced market anxiety. Londoners feel that this is a concrete step towards international currency stability. The biggest reaction in the stock market today was the market's attention to gold mining stocks. The stock prices of gold mines in South Africa, Western Australia, and Western Africa have all risen. US securities are also firm, but British first-class securities and railway stocks have been sold, intending to obtain funds for future speculation. Textile stocks are looser than before, the reason being the anxiety that competition between US and Japanese textiles will intensify, as it is expected that Japan may further depress its currency value. In the foreign exchange market, the pound sterling is weaker than other gold currencies. The reason seems to be the large-scale purchase of gold and gold coins by the Americans in London and other places. Although President Roosevelt's message does not contain anything that would allow Americans to sell their silver, silver prices are now showing signs of loosening. The market price of British goods is in sympathy with the US market and is also higher than before. (16th Reuters)

British Cabinet Discusses Trade Impact

Or Will Increase Tariffs

To Prevent US Goods from Being Dumped

(London) The British Cabinet will discuss the impact of the dollar devaluation on British trade at its regular meeting today and will seek to prevent US goods from being dumped in the British Empire. It is reported that if the British Cabinet sees a continuous influx of US goods, it will increase the current tax rates or levy new taxes on goods that were previously tax-free. All decided measures will invite the cooperation of various autonomous regions to achieve practical results. According to financial circles here, President Roosevelt's message to Congress yesterday will at least put the gold standard in a temporary predicament. According to a source close to the Bank of England, the US dollar, after being reduced in content in accordance with President Roosevelt's message, will make US goods more competitive in foreign trade. This move will force the countries that are still clinging to the gold standard to compete to depress their currency values. President Roosevelt's message caused great surprise in London. The opening exchange rate of the pound against the US dollar was 5.15, which then fell to 5.15 1/2. According to financial circles here, the US dollar, after being devalued by 6 shillings, will allow the pound to reach 5.45, or even continue to fall. (16th National Telegram)

French Finance Minister Concerned about the Franc

May Affect the Pound

Believes It Does No Harm to the Franc

(Paris) After President Roosevelt's message on currency was sent to Congress, Finance Minister Bonnet held an important meeting with his staff and Mr. Jillot, a member of the Bank of France, to discuss the impact of the US monetary policy. Those responsible believe that the US President's message may affect the pound, but not only is the franc completely unharmed, but its value is also becoming more and more solid, and even foreign capitalists will regard it as a more stable currency and be happy to purchase it. (15th Havas)

Japanese Government Worries About the Future

Advocates Changing Gold Production Policy

Decline of Japanese Exchange Rate Affects Our Country

(Tokyo) The government, concerned about the future of the Japanese-American exchange rate due to the United States' implementation of devaluation, intends to establish a strategy for stabilizing the exchange rate. The Ministry of Finance also attaches great importance to this issue and is determined to study its methods. Within the Ministry of Finance, opinions advocating for changing the domestic gold production policy and re-establishing the fundamental principles of the gold policy, as well as adopting a system of purchasing domestic gold and averaging exchange rate funds, are gradually gaining strength. That is, the current foreign exchange management system only aims to suppress exchange rate speculation and does not have the function of actively stabilizing exchange rates. Therefore, it is necessary to implement new measures to prevent future rises in Japanese gold prices and stabilize fluctuations in exchange rates. However, Finance Minister Takahashi has always opposed artificial exchange rate stabilization policies. Therefore, which method will ultimately be adopted is attracting much attention from all parties. (16th, Associated Press)

(China United Press, local dispatch) According to a certain banker, the Japanese exchange rate has continued to fall for days. Today, one hundred yen is only worth eighty-six yuan in national currency. Therefore, it is more advantageous to transport Japanese goods to China. Japan's exchange rate dumping policy poses a great blow to the future of our country's promotion of domestic goods. At today's exchange rate, one yuan of Japanese goods only sells for eighty-six cents in our country, which is still very cost-effective. If our government does not take early measures to deal with this, the future of domestic goods will be unimaginable. Japanese merchants expect the Japanese exchange rate to fall to around seventy yuan.

US Treasury Secretary Indicates Continued Intent to Borrow Money

If US-UK-France Agreement is Reached

International Currency Prices Will be Stabilized

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that the government still intends to borrow $1 billion, but the profits from the devaluation of the dollar can be used to cover government expenses. The Treasury Department intends to receive all of the gold owned by the Financial Rehabilitation Corporation at the old price of $20.67 per ounce, with the losses borne by the members of the Rehabilitation Corporation. Morgenthau also stated that he believes that the agreement between the United States, Britain, and France is sufficient to promote the stabilization of international currency prices. American gold reserves can be allocated to other countries in the form of commercial credit. If France abandons the gold standard, it will hinder American monetary policy because it will change the price of gold. The government has now issued an executive order prohibiting the export of all American legal tender, such as silver coins, unless licensed. Foreign exchange transactions and credit transfers required for ordinary commerce may continue as before without a license. Senator Thomas told people that this is a more extensive inflationary action than any inflationary advocate has hoped for. American currency and silver can all be nationalized in the same way as gold. Some silver auxiliary coins will continue to circulate, but a large amount of silver will be stored in the national treasury as preparation for issuing banknotes. The New York Sun reported that most bankers and economists believe that a fourteen-cent devaluation of the dollar is still too small. (16th, Reuters)

Tragic Plane Crash on the Way Back From Saigon, Ten Passengers Killed, Governor-General of Vietnam Also Among the Victims, Frozen Parts and Malfunctioning Operation Were the Cause of the Crash

(Paris) The French long-distance flight team, led by General Veilman, successfully flew in Africa and returned to France. It arrived at Le Bourget airfield near Paris in the afternoon. People in the French capital were elated and prepared to celebrate enthusiastically. Unexpectedly, the bad news of the "Jade" arrived in the evening, shocking everyone. The plane was flying back to France from Saigon when it crashed near Corbigny. All ten passengers, including Governor-General of Vietnam Pasquier, were tragically killed, and people were deeply saddened. The ceremony planned to welcome the Veilman flight team was cancelled altogether. The details of the incident are recorded below:

The "Jade" plane, carrying Governor-General of Vietnam Pasquier, Commerce Director Xu Mi of the Aviation Department and his wife, took off from Athens at 7:00 AM today, arrived in Marseille at 2:23 PM, and departed again at 3:10 PM. It then arrived in Lyon at 4:20 PM, and at 6:15 PM, it flew towards Paris again. At 7:10 PM, the "Jade" sent a radio message reporting wind and snow along the way. At 8:45 PM, the Corbigny police reported that the plane had crashed and caught fire. Residents of the Corbigny area rushed to the rescue, but the fire was fierce and unavoidable, and there was no way to save them. Pasquier, Xu Mi and his wife, pilot Lu Nai, radio operator Kan Bai'er, mechanic Gailan, director of the airline's technical team Basailuke, director of the business team Nogai, technician Ci Lio, and Pasquier's adjutant Pu Lusu, a total of ten people, were all burned to charcoal. Aviation Minister Gu Tuo, upon hearing the news, immediately went to the scene of the accident by car with Deputy Minister Tellesar for inspection. It is believed that the "Jade" was flying in wind and snow, and the weather was very cold, causing some parts to freeze and malfunction, resulting in the accident. According to reports, the "Jade" had previously set a flight record last year. It departed from Saigon a few days ago to fly back to France, and was forced to land near Pos Tao due to damaged parts. Governor-General Pasquier then switched to another plane to fly to Damascus in Syria. After the "Jade" was repaired, he took it back to his country, but unexpectedly suffered a tragic accident. (15th, Havas)

Details of the Accident

◎ Corbigny City: The French commercial flying large monoplane "Jade," carrying Governor-General of Vietnam Pasquier and Commerce Director Xu Mi of the Aviation Department, etc., was flying back to Paris from Saigon when it crashed in Corbigny City, 200 kilometers from Paris, last night. Further details are as follows:

A Loud Crash and the Plane Caught Fire

Last night, the "Jade" plane flew over Corbigny at a very low altitude. At 7:40 PM, a loud crash was suddenly heard. Within seconds, the entire plane caught fire and broke into thousands of hundreds of red-hot pieces, scattered everywhere. The skeleton of the fuselage was thrown fifty meters away from the crash site, showing the intensity of the explosion. The fuselage was burning fiercely and impossible to approach. Although attempts were made to rescue the passengers who were burned to ashes, it was too late. The military police rushed to the scene and only managed to retrieve some pieces of paper and personal belongings from the plane. The military police then tried to maintain order to prevent crowds of curious onlookers from touching the charred bodies of the passengers and the wreckage of the plane. As for the details of the accident, they will not be known until a few days later, or may even remain a mystery forever.

Lightning Flashed, Snow Fell, and the Wind Helped the Fire

However, it is generally said that the weather was unusually bad yesterday, with strong winds, lightning in the sky, and rain and snow alternating. According to the mayor of Corbigny and others who witnessed the accident, one wing of the "Jade" caught fire and separated from the fuselage, still flying a long distance before falling to the ground. Others said that the plane's radio antenna drooped below the fuselage and connected to the current in front of the plane, causing an electrical fire.

The Cause of the Accident Still Needs Investigation

Others who heard the explosion said that the plane crashed due to the explosion of the oxygen cylinder used to start the engine. However, the exact cause will only be determined after an official investigation. It is reported that the "Jade" had previously been piloted by the aviator Tao Lei for various tests, and had also undergone 150 hours of continuous flight. (16th, Havas)

League of Nations Administrative Council Discusses Saar Problem as Focus, Germany Declares Refusal to Send Representatives to Meeting of Technical Cooperation Group for China

(Berlin) Although the League of Nations Administrative Council has formally notified Germany that it will prepare for the 1935 plebiscite in the Saar region this week, German Chancellor Hitler has stated today that Germany does not want to send representatives to Geneva. According to sources close to the government, Germany has no reason to change its bystander attitude towards the League of Nations. Germany has already advocated for the immediate return of the Saar region last year. If it sends representatives to Geneva to listen to plans for the Saar region plebiscite, wouldn't that be self-contradictory? (Geneva) The most politically relevant matter at today's meeting of the League of Nations Administrative Council was the speech by French representative Massigli. He repeatedly requested that Germany be able to participate when the Saar region plebiscite issue is discussed in the League of Nations. It is generally believed here that France's move shows a bright attitude and expresses goodwill towards Germany. Even though Germany has withdrawn from the League of Nations, there is no harm in treating France with the same goodwill. Moreover, regarding the withdrawal from the League of Nations, it will only be possible to actually leave after a two-year period from the notification of withdrawal. Germany notified its withdrawal last October. Now, when discussing the Saar issue, which is most relevant to that country, how can Germany not send representatives to participate? This matter can also be exemplified by Japan. Japan has also notified its withdrawal, but Japan still sends representatives to participate in various shareholder meetings or committees of the League of Nations that are related to its interests. In addition, France's expression is intended to protect the interests of all countries on the one hand, and to make it easier for all countries to exchange opinions on the other hand. If Germany ignores this, then it cannot later accuse the Administrative Council of disregarding Germany and its interests. French Foreign Minister Pongu can arrive on Wednesday. Before Pongu arrives, Massigli will first meet with British representative Eden and Italian representative Aroasia. What they will discuss will likely be the ongoing disarmament negotiations and the various issues listed on the Administrative Council's agenda. (15th, Havas)

⊙ Bombay: Most of India has suffered an unprecedentedly severe earthquake, with at least two hundred dead and huge property losses. The earthquake area extends from Gujarat in the west to eastern Bengal, and from Madras to the Himalayas and Punjab. Its epicenter seems to be about 1,000 miles east of Bombay and 100 miles northwest of Calcutta. Ninety people have been sent to hospitals in Patna, where many households have been displaced. The dead and injured are now mostly buried in the rubble. Gaya suffered as much damage as Patna, but details are not yet known. The roof of the Gamalpur railway station collapsed on a train just as it was entering, killing and injuring several people. Four thousand houses collapsed in Kanpur, and seven thousand were damaged. Many people were bathing in the Ganges when they suddenly felt the river water surging and rushed to the shore. A small earthquake was also felt in Bombay, but there was no damage. (15th, Reuters)

⊙ Calcutta: Official telegrams are pouring in from various parts of India reporting on the earthquake disaster. The most houses were destroyed in Patna and the surrounding villages, totaling 4,000. Another earthquake was felt this morning, but its intensity was moderate, but people were very frightened. There have been a total of thirteen earthquakes since last night. The losses today were not great. (16th, Reuters)

Situation of the Recovery of Xiamen｜Du Qiyun Has Sent Personnel to Mobilize in Zhangzhou and Quanzhou

(Xiamen Correspondence) After the establishment of the pseudo-government in Fujian Province, the people of Fujian Province and overseas Chinese have appealed to the central government to eliminate the rebels as soon as possible. In order to quickly resolve the matter, the central government commissioned Du Qiyun, the former commander of the 17th Army, as a special military envoy in Fujian, to preside over the coordinated suppression at the same time as the dispatch of troops to attack and suppress. After receiving the order, Du, along with Sun Xiangfu, Wu Zhaohua, Xie De, Yang Tianyu, Wan Sheng, etc., arrived in Gulangyu on the 2nd and immediately deployed everything to prepare for resolving the rebel troops stationed in Xiamen and recovering Xiamen Island. It was originally planned to launch on the 5th, but because the navy stationed in Xiamen was concerned that the local people would inevitably suffer losses in the bloodshed after the military launch, Lin Guogeng, commander of the Xiamen Fortress, discussed a peaceful solution with Du. Du also expressed sympathy for this, saying that the purpose of this military action was to disarm the rebel troops and recover Xiamen. He has always been concerned about the welfare of the local area. It would be best to avoid disturbing the local area. Therefore, the original plan was changed, and the navy persuaded Huang Qiang to give up voluntarily, but it was delayed for several days without results. On the 9th, the rebel troops stationed in Xiamen received a telegram from Cai Tingkai ordering them to resist to the end. Du knew that the rebel side was capricious and decided to eliminate them by force. At 12:00 that night, he ordered all the plainclothes teams to be dispatched. The deployment was as follows: (1) 100 plainclothes team members divided to destroy the rebel troops' transportation, cut off their military telephone lines, and occupy the telephone and telegraph offices and the enemy's transportation agencies. (1) 120 Mauser teams, carrying hand grenades, surrounded the rebel company headquarters in Houyuan Township. (1) Two platoons of patrol teams and 60 Mauser teams, carrying bombs, surrounded the rebel camp headquarters in Houyuan Township. (1) One platoon of patrol teams and 30 Mauser teams, carrying bombs, surrounded the rebel troops in Puyuan. (Two platoons) Two platoons of patrol teams and 40 Mauser teams surrounded the rebel troops in Hulian Township. (1) A total of 100 patrol teams and Mauser teams surrounded the rebel company headquarters in Gaoqi Township. (1) One platoon of patrol teams and 30 Mauser teams attacked the rebel troops in Wutong, and plainclothes teams were ambushed on the main roads to block fleeing rebels. (1) More than 300 patrol teams and plainclothes teams were scattered around the areas near Meiren Palace, Douzaiwei, and Zhongshan Park to block the reinforcements in the city. In addition, five companies of patrol teams were concentrated on the heights of Andou Township as a reserve team. On the naval side, the Yongjian and Jiangzhen ships were dispatched at the same time and berthed on the sea off Gaoqi. The Chuqian ship berthed on the sea off Houyu, and the Yixian and Zhongshan ships berthed inside the ports of Wutong and Xiamen City to prevent the rebel troops from crossing the sea to escape and to block the rebel reinforcements from Zhangzhou and Tong'an. After the deployment was completed, at 1:00 AM on the 10th, an order was issued to launch all the routes simultaneously. Initially, the rebel army used delaying tactics to perfunctorily advise the navy. They did not expect the punitive expeditionary army to take such a swift and sudden action. They were caught off guard. Sun Xiangfu, Zhang Lianzhi, Lin Shaoqiu, Jian Jifeng, Xie Liang, etc., personally went to Huang's camp to announce everything. Everyone bowed their heads in submission and obeyed the reorganization. A total of three infantry companies, one company of military police (complete with firearms), one machine gun company (six machine guns and three automatic rifles), and one special service team were reorganized by Xie Jingbo, commander of the 1st Provisional Brigade of the punitive expeditionary army under the jurisdiction of Du. On the morning of the 10th, the Fujian Military Special Envoy Office of the Military Commission was established in Xiamen. All the agencies occupied by the rebel party were recovered at the same time. It was originally planned that 600 plainclothes team members, each carrying short guns and bombs, would surround and confiscate the puppet municipal government guards and the public security bureau security team. Later, because the rebel party fled, their teams and firearms were easily resolved. The city was as peaceful as usual. The citizens were extremely happy with Du's speed in resolving the military situation in Xiamen. On the 11th, the Special Envoy Office ordered the Second Regiment of the punitive Xie Jingbo Brigade to go to recover Kinmen. There were not many rebel troops in the area, and it was resolved within two hours. In recent days, the special operations team of the Political Department of the Special Envoy Office and the militia from Zhangzhou and Quanzhou have been mobilized to various places. In addition to Zhangping, Hua'an, and Kinmen being recovered, the rebel troops stationed in various places are currently under siege and attack. Zhangzhou City, the rear of the rebel army, is in a state of panic. On the 11th, all private cars were requisitioned, and the troops were moved without a fixed location, seemingly trying to struggle and make a final battle. (January 12
