Reading Q&A

Natural Science and Society (II)

Which science is more important and necessary?

｜Answer to Mr. Yu Wanwang (continued)

As for saying which science we should promote to save China's current predicament, this is still clinging to form and starting from personal subjective fantasy without grasping the facts. The current fact in China is that, on the one hand, the public should urgently learn social sciences to cope with the current historical mission imposed on the public, change the status quo, and open up a new situation; once the old obstacles are removed, we need construction, and what we urgently need are technical talents and natural science knowledge. Saving China is a whole project. Although in the previous stage (destroying the old) and the later stage (building the new), there seems to be some emphasis, as far as the whole is concerned, they are indispensable and inseparable. We really cannot promote one and put down the other, because if so, we will fall into fantasy.

In conclusion, both sciences are urgently needed by Chinese society and occupy the same important and inseparable nature in the project of saving China.

However, in China's current situation, there is no environment for the development of natural science. The development of natural science is determined by the productive forces. China's current productive forces are restricted by production relations, that is, there is no possibility of progress. Therefore, in this garden, natural science loses its conditions for flowering. No matter how you promote it, fantasize, it is all useless. Without a huge industrial base, there are also no laboratories and test halls equipped for these industries. Without these material devices, no scientists will naturally emerge. The decline of natural science in China today is not without reason.

On the contrary, social science has now developed better, which is also due to the current Chinese practice, not due to human likes and dislikes, or subjective promotion.

Therefore, we can only say that studying social science now has better conditions than natural science; now, the objective reality has prompted the public to study social science.

As for which one should be studied from a personal perspective, that is a completely different question and does not need to involve whether the subject itself is important. Because when we study a certain subject, we mainly look at whether our environment is suitable. If you are suitable for studying natural science or social science, you don’t have to ask whether the science is important, just go ahead and study it. But you may think that we are ambiguous, because the environment suitable for studying a certain science has not been explained. Then we can specifically tell you: if you are a rich person, willing to serve, and at the same time lack the foundation and interest in natural science, then go and study social science; if you are very calm, have a foundation, and have the material conditions suitable for natural science, then go and study natural science. However, if you think that the study of these two sciences requires two different brains, you are completely wrong and misunderstand our meaning. The reason why we advocate this is in terms of personal aspirations and social effects. As for the attitude or spirit that should be possessed in studying knowledge, it is the same regardless of the subject.

Furthermore, we see that your letter seems to focus on the "career path" issue, and therefore associate it with the urgent need of the subject. We have to answer this question more ambiguously: whether you learn natural science or social science, there is no "career path," but there is a "career path." The reason is obvious, just take a look at the situation in the real society to understand.

Now we will summarize our main points: (1) There is no distinction between important and unimportant in learning; (2) Our study of a certain subject is determined by the social and personal environment; (3) The "career path" is not related to the subject of study. || Respectfully,

Page 13

Spring and Autumn

Factions

— Xian

Grouping without partisanship, partisanship without grouping. In the Three Dynasties, there were "groups" and "parties," but no "factions." In the twentieth century, there are "parties" but no "groups," but there are "factions." I wonder if the "factions" of the twentieth century are what was called "groups" in the Three Dynasties. I am afraid that this public case will be difficult to clear up even if the twenty-four histories of China and the West are turned over. Because in the ancient tombs of Lu and Yu provinces, no anecdotes about "groups" seem to have been excavated.

Let's put aside "groups" and "parties" and talk about the most fashionable "factions" of the year.

In the political sphere, there are the "left-wing," the "right-wing," and also the neither left nor right, awkward "neutral faction." There are the "new faction" and the "old faction," and at the same time there is the neither new nor old "conciliation faction." Therefore, if there is no faction, then there will be three factions. But in the United States, there is the "dry faction" that advocates prohibition and the "wet faction" that advocates lifting the ban on alcohol, but there is no neither dry nor wet "fence-sitting faction." This is an exception.

In China, it is even more interesting. The loud and cheerful Peking Opera naturally belongs to the "ancient faction." The civilized drama that does not jump, does not sing, and does not wear painted faces naturally counts as the "new faction." But between these two factions, there is another faction, neither ancient nor new, which is not called the "neutral faction," the "conciliation faction," or the "fence-sitting faction," but instead it is called the "Shanghai faction." Although this also divides the world into three in the opera world, the name "Shanghai faction" seems somewhat irrelevant to the other factions.

Those who practice acrobatics have the "Wudang faction" and the "Shaolin faction," but the third faction has set up its own banner and is called the "Jianghu faction." Speaking of this "Jianghu faction," it is an all-encompassing group. Catching teeth worms and fortune-telling is the "Jianghu faction," and treating camels is also the "Jianghu faction." Spending money when you have it, and showing off when you don't is indeed the "Jianghu faction," and playing with a large goldfish bowl in your crotch is also the "Jianghu faction." The three religions, nine streams, and eighteen tunes can all be classified into the "Jianghu faction." The "Jianghu faction" naturally does not only represent those who practice acrobatics. This shows that the composition of "factions" in China is "another faction," not the red-haired ghosts, quick-legged ghosts, etc… whose backs can be seen.

Chinese and Western Music

— Shi Ying

"Though I am not as intelligent as Shi Kuang, I understand the refined meaning from hearing string and song." Zhou Yu's words are truly wonderful! We are naturally not as clever as Zhou Yu, but when we look at (not listen to) Chinese and Western music, we can also taste its refined meaning!

▼Huqin and Violin. The huqin and the violin are both stringed instruments. But those who play the violin are renowned musicians whose voices captivate audiences, poets, and professors at music schools. Those who play the huqin are laborers singing bawdy songs, blind musicians accompanying courtesans, mischievous children, and delinquents. It's not that the huqin is inferior to the violin. The violin is a foreign thing, and foreign things should be lucky. The huqin, however, is a naturalized domestic product, and Chinese things should be unlucky.

▼Flower Drum and Dancing. On the street, idlers form a circle, leaving an empty space in the middle. Several women dressed in red and green twist their waists and sing in shrill voices. Gongs and drums are played softly. Respected gentlemen smile with disdain. When officials arrive, they fine and expel them. The flower drum is harmful to public morals. But the piano, with its bold and healthy style, is placed in luxurious dance halls and played melodiously. Couples dance on smooth floors like celestial beings. Joyful but not lewd, sad but not wounding, dancing is considered a noble entertainment. Because the flower drum is Chinese, and the piano is Western.

▼Chinese and English. Chinese lyrics should also be unlucky. Those who sing Chinese songs are primary school students, those who sing "Lotus Clapper" are beggars, and those who hum "Drizzling Rain" are prohibited. Singing folk songs in front of moralistic gentlemen will surely result in a slap in the face. However, college students love to hum famous English songs. So-called Harmony's four-part harmony is not much different from the harmony of "Lotus Clapper," yet four-part harmony is used in solemn auditoriums. As for Western love songs, like the famous "How Can I Leave You?", not only is no one prohibiting them, but some people are even promoting them.

Four Manshus

— Chun Liu

Manshu is the so-called Manjushri, a figure in Buddhist scriptures. Some also associate it with the establishment of the Manchu state two hundred years ago, so the name "Manchukuo" is a transliteration of Manshu. The ancestors of the Aisin Gioro clan wanted to use Buddhist power to stabilize their state's foundation, but it seems no one talks about it.

Since the appearance of the remarkably talented and beautiful Su Manshu in the literary world, people have felt a mystical meaning in the word "Manshu," as if this name is more refined. As far as I know, there are actually four Manshus in the world. Besides Xiangshan Su Manshu, there are two monks also named Manshu. One was recently expelled from Baiyun Mountain in Guangzhou. He is from Sichuan and once studied at the China Inner Academy, where he was a disciple of Ouyang Jian of Yihuang, along with Chen Mingshu. He loved to write screen couplets for people. There are four screen paintings he wrote on the upper floor of Ji Ming Temple in Nanjing, which reads "Monk Manshu of the Four Emei Mountains." The other is from Xinghua and once stayed at Pilu Temple in Nanjing. He is over sixty years old and also likes to compose poems, but they really don't have much poetic flavor.

In addition, there is a Manchu named Manshu who once wrote a book called "Tian Zhi Ou Wen," which specializes in describing the old customs of Beijing. His writing style is very elegant and pleasing, but his era is earlier than these three Manshus.

Moonlit Night

— Wei Zhong

At night, carrying a lonely heart, I walked alone up Mount Wutai.

The bright moonlight shone down softly, very bright and very peaceful, like a spring night. But the bald treetops and the patch of withered yellow grass clearly told me that it was already early winter.

Mount Wutai is not very high, strictly speaking, it can only be considered a mound. It is surrounded by deep, dense forests. On the top of the mountain lies a vast, desolate meadow, quiet and secluded. It is simple and pure, like a village girl. What's more, there is a crescent moon, curved like moth eyebrows, shining its clear light across the clear sky.

This place is located in the center of the capital's urban area. In theory, there should be many citizens who are weary of the city's bustling life and need this quiet place to lie in the embrace of nature and enjoy its great caress! However, besides my lonely figure, there is no one else here. Is this beautiful scenery and wonderful time arranged for this solitary wanderer to enjoy alone?

Deep indigo villages lie scattered and dormant in the night. Occasionally, one or two starlight fires flicker between the farmhouses.

At Confucius Temple: Perhaps the intoxicating Jazz King is being screened in the cinema, and perhaps the mesmerizing "Traveling Dragon Playing with Phoenix" is being sung at Tianyun Pavilion! The young masters are probably indulging in singing and dancing at this moment!

The strong electric light of the probing lights, like a strong swimming dragon, contains great ambition and searches the wilderness for its purpose of aggression, constantly sweeping over from the imperialist warships at Xiaguan.

Suddenly, it seemed like some voices were coming from the left corner. Passing around a row of trees, under the faint moonlight, a young couple sat side by side in a grass pavilion.

The rustling cold wind blew sharply.

"Cold?" "My love!"

"No, I don't feel it at all!"

Tender greetings scattered in the quiet night air, very light and very beautiful. The girl lowered her head, looking at the large, desolate meadow in front of her. On the meadow, the moonlight and dense fog merged into one, drifting white and misty.

Everything was silent. But is this a time for silence?

"What a beautiful moonlit night!"

Looking... slowly one hand bent over, hand in hand, the flame of youth burned fiercely in the hearts of the young couple, two bodies moved, two souls danced together, two people hugged tightly!

What a sharp demonstration to a lonely wanderer. Holding my wounded heart, I sneaked back along the slanted path.

Spoiled children of love, I wish you eternal happiness!

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty: Whispering Before the Lamp, Painstakingly Instructing the Weak Child; Leaning on a Cane to Wander Down the Mountain, Observing Heroes with a Cold Eye

When Zhao Weng heard what he said, he thought he had seen the women being teased on the platform, so he made some remarks. Now the more he spoke, the more complaints he had, and he himself was drawn into the vortex, clearly directing his remarks at something. This was quite puzzling, so he looked at him and said with a smile, "Mr. Gan, did you also fail because of some love affair?" Only then did Ji Zhi realize that the woman he could not get was this old man's daughter-in-law. How could he clearly say it out? He smiled and shook his head twice and said, "It's not worth talking about! Don't mention it, let's sit and drink a little and look at the red leaves." If he hadn't said this, Zhao Weng would have thought he had guessed a little. Now that he didn't want to delve deeper, Zhao Weng understood that there was a great secret inside. Talking was naturally out of the question, but he couldn't forget this matter in his heart.

Chapter Twenty-Three

The Pain Is Unbearable, Listening Attentively to Drums and Music; The Joyful Feeling Is Not Satisfied, Hastening to Part with a Flying Talisman

At this moment, Ji Zhi realized that he had spoken too quickly. How could he complain about his son's affairs in front of his father? So he smiled at Zhao Weng and said, "Old master, I was out of my mind just now, you don't have to believe those words. When young people have a woman, many storms will arise. Without a woman, they will become jealous when they see other people's women." If he hadn't clarified, Zhao Weng would have been suspicious, but after he clarified, Zhao Weng was even more suspicious. His wrinkled face turned red, and the few white pockmarks hidden inside his skin were all highlighted. (293)

Short Story

A Certain Blind Man

— Hui Jian

In this village, no one knew him, and no one knew where he came from. His eyes were dull, his fixed eyeballs, white with circles of blue, just like the eyes of a dead fish we see on a plate, completely fixed.

When he first came, he lived in a dilapidated Earth God Temple. Later, he was taken in by Liu Village, but was soon sent back to the Earth God Temple. The reason was that Mr. Four in Liu Village discovered his Shandong accent and questioned him about his origins. He refused to say a word, but rudely asked Mr. Four and everyone else:

"Do you know if Marco Rishi is still alive?"

Mr. Four asked in surprise, "Who is Marco Rishi? Who is Marco Rishi? What is his relationship to you?"

He was silent and smiled, his smile filled with sarcasm and arrogance. Mr. Four suppressed his anger and gave him a satisfying lunch, hoping to get some truth from his generous treatment, but after he was full, he patted his stomach and asked:

"Does anyone do a good deed and tell me... is Marco Rishi still alive?"

Mr. Four sent him back to the Earth God Temple, saying, "If you don't let me know who you are, I won't help you."

He did not resist this treatment. He smiled and returned to the Earth God Temple, found the niche where he used to sleep, and quietly lay down by himself.

Every day at a certain time, he came out to beg for food. He wrapped himself in a dirty, ragged robe covered in clumps of rotten floss, and held a walking stick made of pine branches less than two feet long.

He listened carefully to the footsteps of all passers-by. He had the special wisdom to distinguish what kind of person each footstep belonged to. He sometimes stretched out his other free hand to stop the kind person he imagined, but he did not ask for money but said urgently:

"Sir, tell me, is Marco Rishi still alive?"

People pushed him away impatiently, and walked away quickly, or left a copper coin in his hand, telling him, "I don't know who Marco Rishi is, just as I don't know who you are."

Then he sadly retracted his hand, turned his lychee-like eyes, and returned to where he was standing, smiling bitterly.

Once he had finished touring the village, and almost everyone had been troubled by his Marco Rishi question, he officially visited Mr. Four of Liu Village, asking him to provide him with a last amount of dry food, and explaining that he was about to leave the village immediately.

"Are you going to continue looking for your Marco Rishi?"

Mr. Four asked him.

"Yes, I'm looking for him. I've been looking for him for five years, and I can look for him for another five years. In this remaining painful life of mine, only he can save me..."

Mr. Four unexpectedly became clever and quickly asked him, "Save you! I know; is he a foreign ophthalmologist?"

"An ophthalmologist, yes, and a missionary. Xu Laojiu in our village told me this. He saw with his own eyes this foreign doctor cure two blind people in Macheng. He just poured a little yellow water from the silver bottle and washed it on their eyelids, and in less than three days, they could all see. That foreign living immortal doesn't want us to repay him, maybe he just wants me to convert... I'm willing, I've learned it, singing hymns, if he is willing to cure my eyes, I can sacrifice anything."

Hearing these magical words, Mr. Four became even more excited. Based on his suspicions, he blurted out, "I'm very surprised. I've also been to Macheng, and not only have I not heard of such an ophthalmologist, but even Marco Rishi, this name is very unfamiliar to me. Can you believe that Xu Laojiu would not deceive you?" (To be continued)

Education News - Outlying Areas

Progress of Education in Zhejiang Province in the Past Six Months ▲ Director Chen Reports to the Provincial Government ▲ Quality and Quantity Have Increased

Chen Bulei, Director of the Zhejiang Education Department, reported to the provincial government yesterday on the work of the department in the past six months, stating briefly that the department regarded promoting the improvement of local education in various counties and cities as an important part of its work. The education in counties and cities in the past six months can be divided into two aspects: quality improvement and quantity increase. Regarding quality improvement, the important aspects are the three types of methods promulgated by the department, namely: (1)

Randomly test primary school students. All students in grades three and above in primary schools are tested as necessary, based on the inspection results of inspectors in various counties and cities, either temporarily in each school or in a gathering in one place, to conduct random tests of the students of the school, but in order to understand the actual performance of a certain grade or subject in the entire county, a general random test can also be held by region. (2) Encourage teachers to continue their studies. Teachers' further education methods are divided into four categories: A. Gathering further education, such as holding holiday lectures, primary school subject research meetings; B. Reading further education, such as organizing reading clubs, setting up correspondence research departments, placing mobile libraries; C. Observation further education, such as going abroad to visit teaching demonstrations, holding exhibitions; D. Others, such as special topic discussions, celebrity lectures, etc.; (3) Train primary school principals, also divided into four points: A. Study and implement various education laws and regulations, and various administrative orders related to education; B. Lecture on the most needed subjects in recent education; C. Based on the inspection results, for common or special shortcomings, matters that should be corrected, and improvement methods; D. Discuss how to closely connect with the society and the public. The above methods stipulate that each county and city should hold at least once a year. As for the promotion of quantity, it is also divided into three items: (1) Increase the number of township primary schools. In the past six months, 269 townships in various counties without schools have increased their number, and 187 townships with schools have expanded their number. (2) Consolidate school funds and school property. The education funds of various counties in the province were originally extremely strained. Now, affected by the rural economic decline, they have been tightened repeatedly. At this unavoidable time, in terms of opening up sources, we can only follow the provisions of Article 2 of the Administrative Yuan's Measures for Guaranteeing Local Education Funds, and request the provincial government to designate and allocate 20% of the newly added local taxes in the future to fill local education funds. This case has been approved by the provincial government and agreed by the Finance Department. (3) Stipulate supervision methods. The Education Department recently promulgated the "Measures for County Education Bureau Chiefs to Go to the Countryside for Inspection." The matters to be paid attention to during the inspection include eight points, the most important of which are A. Convene township chiefs and deputies in the locality to hold talks or meetings on promoting the increase of schools and enriching enrollment; B. Examine the inspection reports of county supervisors or instructors as the basis for formulating the next inspection plan; C. Examine the education status of various townships and districts, plan to raise funds and promote consolidation; D. Visit gentry who are enthusiastic about education and exchange opinions on improving education.

Publication of Historical Diplomatic Materials from the Late Qing Dynasty

Foreign aggression has reached its peak. In tracing its origins, everything started in the late Qing Dynasty. The "Historical Diplomatic Materials from the Late Qing Dynasty," compiled by Huang Yunsheng and Wang Yunchou, father and son, meticulously detail the process of establishing various unequal treaties, records of meetings between the Zongli Yamen (foreign ministry) and foreign envoys, as well as wartime negotiations, treaty consultations, the demarcation of the Northwest border, and the deployment of Southeast defenses. The collection is comprehensive and meticulous in every word. Much of the content is not found in archives, making it a rare and monumental diplomatic work.

Temporary Postponement of the Boy Scout Council's Relocation

The Shanghai Boy Scout Council, due to the cramped conditions of its current location within Shangwen Primary School, which is insufficient for its needs, had requested the Shanghai Bureau of Education to allocate the old site on Daji Road as the council's new premises. The Shanghai Bureau of Education approved the allocation of the former Fourth Section's buildings at the old site to the council. However, the council found the Fourth Section's buildings still too small, so they have temporarily postponed the relocation and will continue to operate within Shangwen Primary School. Now that the Municipal Party Headquarters has moved to the old Municipal Government site, the council will submit a request to move into the old Municipal Party Headquarters site for office purposes.

Physical Education

Editing Committee Meeting for Detailed Items of Physical Education Instruction in Primary and Secondary Schools ▲ Work Assignments and Deadlines for Submissions

(Nanjing, 16th) The Ministry of Education's Editing Committee for Outlines of Physical Education Instruction in Primary and Secondary Schools held its second meeting on the morning of the 16th. Chaired by Hao Gengsheng, the following resolutions were made: (1) Revised and approved the physical education goals for senior and junior high schools and elementary schools; (2) Revised and approved the types of physical education materials for each level of school, and the allocation methods; (3) Stipulated the writing format, using simple classical Chinese and new-style punctuation for typesetting; (4) Changed the "Instructional Outline" to "Detailed Instructional Items"; (5) Assigned work: Chen Yingmei and Chen Kui were responsible for editing elementary school materials, Wu Yunrui and Song Junfu for junior high school, and Cheng Dengke and Wu Cheng for senior high school; (6) Submission deadlines: end of May for elementary school, end of March for junior high school, and end of August for senior high school, all to be submitted to Wu Yunrui for review; (7) Schools with sufficient financial resources for physical education equipment should strictly follow the provisions of the National Physical Education Implementation Plan for equipment; those unable to do so should, at a minimum, equip themselves according to the detailed items compiled by this committee. It is also reported that these detailed items will be printed in three large volumes, one each for elementary, junior high, and senior high schools, each estimated to be over 120,000 words.

Miss Helen Jacobs Elected as the 1933 American Sports Queen

▲ Elected by 180 Journalists

▲ Miss Helen Elected with 64 Votes

▲ Mrs. Moody Seventh with Only Three Votes

(New York News) Miss Helen Jacobs, last year's American women's tennis champion and a key player in the Anglo-American Wightman Cup, has been elected as the 1933 American "Sports Queen" with 64 votes. In this election, voted by 180 sports journalists in New York, Miss Helen Jacobs was honored with the title of 1933 "Sports Queen" with more than one-third of the total votes, which is no easy feat. Miss Van Wie, the national women's golf champion, ranked second with 48 votes. Mrs. Moody, the world-renowned tennis queen, received only three votes. Miss Didrickson, the all-around athlete who was elected queen in 1932, received only two votes. The rankings are as follows:

(1) Helen Jacobs (National Tennis Championship) 64 votes

(2) Virginia Van Wie (National Golf Championship) 48 votes

(3) Lenore Kight (National Freestyle Swimming Championship) 31 votes

(4) Katherine Rawls (National Swimming Championship) 16 votes

(5) Harper Hord (Golfer) 5 votes

(6) Helen Hicks (Golfer) 4 votes

(7) Mrs. Moody (Wimbledon Tennis Championship) 3 votes

Jinan Winter Ball Games: Nine Classics Wins Senior Basketball Championship

Finals Result in 23 to 18 Victory Over First Strong

Two Armed Athletes Clash in a Fierce Battle

(Jinan Correspondence) The peaks of Thousand Buddha Mountain are covered in pure white snow, contrasting with the green pines and cypresses, unfolding a natural painting. The thin sunlight breaks through the morning mist and slowly rises. The crows on the trees also fly and caw. This is truly a "winter morning" at the sports field.

The winter ball games initiated by the Provincial Stadium were originally scheduled for seven weeks but were extended by two weeks due to rain and snow. Apart from the junior basketball championship won by Rural Teachers and the junior football championship won by Donglu, and the senior football championship won by Jingcheng, only the senior basketball finals between Nine Classics and First Strong were held today (the 11th). With the final battle concluded, the event reached a successful conclusion, and the winter ball games came to a complete end.

This morning at 9:30, the two teams met at the Provincial Stadium. The Nine Classics team, representing the 20th Division's mortar regiment, consisted of tall and strong players. Since their debut, they had fought dozens of battles, encountering no worthy opponents. The First Strong team, representing the 1st Regiment of the Pistol Brigade, was short, agile, and had long enjoyed a prestigious reputation in Jinan. The clash between these two armed athletes on the field, vying for the championship, was expected to be intense.

The strength of both sides was balanced, with the lead changing hands frequently. First Strong's Wang Shengcai played like a dragon or tiger, shooting from both long and short distances with ease, increasing the score steadily. Seeing their performance faltering, Nine Classics shouted encouragement. Guo Xiushan launched subtle and overt attacks, quickly reversing the decline. Nine Classics became increasingly brave, while First Strong repeatedly failed to score, gradually losing ground. At the end of the first half, the score was 17 to 11, with Nine Classics taking the lead.

After a break, First Strong regrouped and vowed to counterattack with all their might. Hei Shigong scored first under the basket, and Wang Shengcai made a solo raid, returning in triumph. At this moment, Nine Classics ambushed from all sides, regaining two points. Strong soldiers pressed into First Strong's territory, with shouts of men and horses and the sound of drums ringing. First Strong repeatedly replaced players, and although there was a slight improvement, the deficit from the first half was too large, and it was difficult to recover lost ground. The entire game ended with First Strong winning the second half 7 to 6, but the final result was 23 to 18, with Nine Classics winning the championship.

Special Item

Report on Vocational Education from Education Ministry Specialist's European Study

(9)

Within the French vocational education system, there is a system of inspectors. Inspectors are assigned to each province or district. Their duties include inspecting school affairs and serving as a liaison between schools and the economic and industrial sectors, as well as consulting and discussing matters with the central Ministry of Education's supervisors. These inspectors are familiar with local conditions and understand the inner workings of schools. Their insights and ideas are often relevant and key, making them a significant aid to the recent development and notable success of French vocational education.

French laws stipulate that all vocational school administrators must have close contact with the economic sector, and all teaching staff and factory training instructors must spend part of their school holidays visiting manufacturing factories for observation or practical training to ensure that school and factory methods align with current trends.

As mentioned above, vocational schools are indeed school organizations that are good at adapting to the environment, full of activity, and evolving with the times. Only in this way can they operate smoothly within the national economic life, facing ever-changing and complex conditions.

Vocational Education Organization

The French vocational education organization is divided into two departments: employment guidance and vocational training. Vocational training is further divided into three levels: apprentice training, middle-level cadre training, and senior-level cadre training. The training work at each level is either undertaken by the government or organized by private individuals.

Nearly 80% of the national population works in the industrial sector. To have the government bear the entire responsibility is economically unrealistic, so it is necessary to encourage and motivate multi-faceted cooperation. The following is a description of schools jointly run by the French central government and local or provincial governments, such as municipal administrative committees or provincial administrative committees, followed by schools run by private individuals.

(1) Employment Guidance

When male and female students across the country leave elementary school at the age of 12 or 13, they, or their parents, must be given detailed guidance regarding future employment paths, career advancement opportunities, physical and intellectual requirements, and difficulties. This guidance, according to the provisions of the 1922 decree, is the responsibility of the employment guidance bureaus established in various regions, which provide the public with the necessary knowledge for employment.

To ensure detailed work, the employment guidance bureaus must cooperate with the following departments: (1) elementary school teachers, who provide information on students' usual intelligence and conduct; (2) doctors, who examine students' physical fitness; (3) labor union introduction agencies, which report on the local demand for artisans, so that young people can avoid mistakenly entering fields with oversupply and be guided into careers with better prospects.

In 1928, the Institute of Employment Guidance was established in Paris, dedicated to the investigation and research of employment guidance issues to achieve perfection. Currently, there are over a hundred employment guidance bureaus established nationwide in France, demonstrating the importance attached to this issue by the French authorities in charge of vocational education.

(2) Vocational Training

(A) Apprentice Training

Any young person who has just left elementary school and wants to learn a craft to make a living must receive apprentice training. Therefore, those from poor families enter factories or shops, while those from slightly wealthier families enter apprentice schools. Both are places for apprentice training.

Free Talk

The Beijing School and the Shanghai School

— Cao Juren

Mr. Shen Congwen, in the 32nd issue of the literary supplement of the Dagongbao, spoke freely about the ugliness of Shanghai School writers. He said that the combination of "reputation and talent" and "commercial competition" constitutes our current concept of the term "Shanghai School." … Let us extend it, "opportunistic," "weather-vane," … this is what is called the Shanghai School; gathering some new literati, meeting together, or talking about Greece and Rome, or talking about writers and women, … getting some money from the government, then eating, drinking, and organizing some literary gatherings, recruiting disciples, deceiving readers, … this is what is called the Shanghai School. Emotionally leaning left, brave as a lion, but immediately surrendering and confessing when the situation is wrong, and identifying and harming friends, seeking credit and profit, this is what is called the Shanghai School. Because of a thirst for fame, using various methods outside of their works to flaunt themselves … this is what is called the Shanghai School." He concluded, "Harming the health of new literature, making literature itself weak and powerless, causing the general public to lose the necessary understanding of literature, and often distorting the meaning of literature, and making some young people who are about to engage in literature not focus on practical efforts, thinking that being a celebrity is admirable, not working hard at writing but first trying to be a writer, all of this is the style of these Shanghai School writers." The sins of the Shanghai School are so heinous that even the darkest curses to curse its demise would not be excessive.

However, is today's "Beijing School" different from the "Shanghai School?" "Beijing School" and "Shanghai School" were originally terms in Chinese drama. The Beijing School can be said to be classical, and the Shanghai School can be said to be romantic. The Beijing School is like a lady from a noble family, and the Shanghai School is like a modern girl. "My friend" Mr. Xin Zujian, in discussing Beijing and Shanghai, said, "The Beijing School artist has Dr. Mei to represent, and the Shanghai School artist has Master Liu who is undoubtedly the one." If a lady from a noble family can ridicule a modern girl for showing off her style, then the modern girl can also retort and mock the lady from a noble family for being outdated. If Dr. Mei laughs at Master Liu for selling primitive heads, Master Liu will certainly accuse Dr. Mei of not understanding the Renaissance. Let us discuss the current situation of the Beijing School. Dr. Hu Shi, a brilliant member of the Beijing School, also talks about the history of philosophy, also talks about literary revolution, also runs independent reviews, also rushes around on the Baoding road. Is he different from what Mr. Shen Congwen calls opportunistic? I say: There is no difference. The Shanghai School pretends to be refined, either talking about Greece and Rome or talking about writers and women; while the Beijing School monopolizes refinement, either holding hundredth-week or thousandth-week memorials for Byron, or composing dozens or hundreds of regulated poems in the style of "Autumn Thoughts," confined in a glass room, isolated from reality; are they different from each other? I say there is no difference. Shanghai School writers get some money from the government, organize some literary gatherings, recruit disciples, eat and drink; Beijing School writers get some money from some cultural foundation, travel abroad wildly, and talk about culture; are they different from each other? I say there is no difference. "Once you become a writer, you are not worth watching," all crows are black, and there is no distinction between the "Beijing School" and the "Shanghai School."

Therefore, it is certain that the Shanghai School writers are all bad. However, modern girls wearing high heels walk on the streets, walk in the markets, and walk in the parks; they are always social and in contact with society. Shouldn't those ladies with bound feet hiding in their boudoirs be ashamed? Mr. Shen Congwen wants to call on the Beijing School to sweep away the Shanghai School. I am afraid it is too early to say so! I think tomorrow's critics will definitely not stand in the camp of the Beijing School. Only by adopting a sweeping attitude towards the Shanghai School that goes beyond disregard and contempt, and bravely sweeping away both the Shanghai School and the Beijing School, can we open up the path to new literature!

China today still has no great writers, nor great critics; the lonely literary scene does not allow critics to show their faces, which is why the diary-keeping school is so popular for a time! Alas!

The "Supra-Morality" of Art

— Tang Jun

The "morality" mentioned here refers to the "morality" recognized by "ethicists," "jurists," or the "Bible."

Originally, this issue was no longer an issue in Europe, but Chinese culture has not made progress for a long time. Although China's modern art movement has had a history of one or two decades, to this day, the general public cannot have a correct and appropriate understanding of "nude art." Furthermore, I heard a friend say, "Nude art" is still subject to various social criticisms, so I can't help but want to revisit this old topic and ramble a bit.

The word "morality" already represents something vague and uncertain in common sense. In the art world, it has long changed its original image ｜｜ the image defined by "ethicists," "jurists," and the "Bible." For example, killing is immoral, but a executioner killing a condemned criminal is moral. Knocking down walls is immoral, but some construction workers dismantling walls and even destroying all the magnificent buildings in a finished grand exposition is moral. Looking at Baudelaire's expression of "vice," Zola's depiction of "madness" and "suffering," Rodin's nude female statues with "legs apart and exposed genitals," etc., they have all shattered the stereotyped morality! Their works have all gained immortal value, which shows that morality in art has lost its importance and has become a meaningless thing!

Most superficial people take the morality or immorality of the "subject matter" of art as the basis for art criticism, which is really absurd! Because certain religious or war-themed works can lead the world to religious ideals and beliefs, as well as martial spirit or anti-war concepts, they say that the value of art lies in these moral themes. Because certain descriptions of "licentiousness," "madness," "violence," "theft," or other "vices" may have the danger of leading people astray, they say that this immoral temptation is the reason for the decline of art's value. These are the slogans shouted by the "ethicists" who look dignified and the "priests" who recite the Bible.

However, an artwork is not a "self-cultivation class" ｜｜ "ethics," nor is it a "law" or a "Bible." The "artist" is not an "ethicist," a "lawyer," or a "priest"; how can he be compared with a general model!

Artists have no obligation to persuade people to do good, nor do they have the desire to tempt people to do evil. They do not show their skills in the morality or immorality of the subject matter, but they discover themselves and recognize others similar to themselves through the intensified efforts of creation. They frankly and honestly, without any concealment, depict as much as possible what they feel, whether it is "licentiousness," "jealousy," "theft," "adultery"……… It is considered finished. They do not consider the results of external "feelings" and "influences"! They do not want people to praise them as "sages" or "geniuses"; they are not afraid of people's "sneers," "criticisms," and "curses."

In short, the "morality" that ordinary people consider important has no power in art.

Monologue

— Miao Chongqun

When the night is quiet, I often cannot sleep. My dry eyes hurt when they are open, and they also hurt when they are closed. Anyway, whether they are open or closed, it is the same in the darkness. I don't want to see anything anymore. Light has hurt my eyes and exposed all my bad deeds.

During the day, my mood is irritable, and I cannot be peaceful more than anyone else. For a little incident, I scold and roar. Sometimes I even smash a teacup, and then I smash two more glass cups. My face is flushed, and I am panting. I don't care if the neighbors are laughing at me next door. Only when I have finished venting do I feel a little calmer.

I can't say what the object is. I have nothing of value, only accompanied by a wife who suffers from the same pain as me. She also has no fate that is more fortunate than mine: toiling, suffering, and struggling with the remaining strength: although we eat porridge in the morning and porridge in the evening, it is still difficult to get the rice needed to make porridge.

There is no reason when I roar, but my wife sobs silently on the side, which somehow aroused my tyrannical curses again.

Only those who pursue light are originally people without light;

Now, the night has come, and the neighbors' snores, like the roar of cattle, come from next door. It shows its power, making me feel jealous like fire from the bottom of my heart, but helplessly, I can only toss and turn on the bed, gently, and yet afraid of waking up my wife beside me.

｜｜A poor woman! I seemed to be secretly calling her name in my heart. You are at peace when you are resting. Forget about the things of the day. People who live in the darkness also do not know what is called darkness.

From time to time, my wife suddenly rambles in her sleep. Vaguely saying intermittent sentences, with her heartfelt confession and resentful tone, every word seems to have a great stimulation for me.

I concentrated on listening, and I repented myself, unable to distinguish a single word. I repented sincerely.

Sleep talking is the words of her soul. She doesn't know that her long-depressed soul is talking to me in the dark.

……………………

"Wake up! Wake up!" After being awakened by my wife, I still heard the lingering sound of my crying. I touched my wet face, and I didn't say anything.

Because my wife didn't ask anything either, it made me feel very embarrassed. She doesn't know that her sleep talking made my soul repent, but she also doesn't know what is going on with the person who appears on the human stage as a clown during the day and sobs like a woman at night.

Wells' Prophecy: A Record of the Sino-Japanese War in 1935 (Continued)

— Meng Zhen

As a result, Japan gradually became tired of the war. Farmers only saw their sons go out to join the army, but they didn't see them come home. Coupled with the general shortage of supplies and the scarcity of strong men, disasters occurred. By 1935, there had already been a strong movement for a ceasefire. Later, several strikes occurred in Nagoya, resulting in hundreds of deaths and injuries. In order to purchase military supplies overseas, Japan needed cash, so it tried its best to dump goods abroad. But apart from this, now grains from Canada and the United States, and meat from Australia, have become necessary for Japan. The war thus caused panic in Japan and turned most of China's productive capacity into nothing. During the European war, Germany had an economic miracle, but Japan's social structure was too primitive. It was impossible for Japan to fight difficulties like Germany. Japan's bonds thus continued to fall in price, and even providing a high interest rate of 1.4 to 1.5 cents could not borrow money. But the war still showed no signs of ending.

The Japanese warlords had reached the point of being unable to stop. The people's curses against the war became more and more intense day by day. The United States, Russia, and European countries stared intently. In order to break through this difficult situation of exhaustion and isolation, Japan decided to make a final effort and invade the central part of China with a large army ｜｜ Hubei. After huge preparations, Japan mobilized all the people who could fight to the front line. Japan's military plan was to "strike at the heart of China." So it concentrated on Hubei from three directions: Nanjing, Shandong, and Guangdong. The reason why the Japanese army was divided into these three fronts was to maximize the plunder of materials from the Chinese countryside.

At this time, railway transportation was difficult to maintain, and most of it was non-existent, so transportation was very inconvenient. Therefore, when the Japanese army passed through the border of Hubei Province, one-third of its entire army had to engage in the construction of military roads like a long snake. Under such transportation conditions, naturally the light and heavy artillery that Japan could transport to attack Hubei was not much better than that of the Chinese army. Moreover, behind the Chinese army, there were abundant resources from Sichuan and assistance from Europe and the United States.

The three Japanese armies eventually surrounded Wuchang. This was like a loose ring, which was once gradually tightening, but soon stopped. This was the result of the soldiers being exhausted to the extreme. Therefore, the Japanese encirclement failed to succeed along the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The New Year of 1938 arrived, and Japan was waiting for a victorious war report at home. But from the crescent-shaped long trenches, there was no news. Thus, a year passed in vain.

In July 1938, dysentery and bubonic plague broke out in the Japanese army. The epidemic was very severe, and the Japanese military doctors used all their abilities but still failed to achieve any effect. Therefore, from the beginning of 1939, Japan began to retreat to Nanjing. Because the transportation routes were disrupted everywhere, the losses were very heavy. The truth about the Japanese army's retreat is still known today. In short, of the more than two million troops, less than half were healthy and unharmed when they retreated to Nanjing. The blow that hunger inflicted on the Japanese army was actually more severe than the attacks of the Chinese army and people. Because they were extremely exhausted from hunger, many fell dead on the road of retreat. The reason why there were so few Japanese soldiers taken prisoner at that time was because the Chinese army did not have food to feed the prisoners. The Japanese army thus retreated to Nanjing under the attack of hunger, fatigue, and epidemic, with no more than 100,000 people. The roads were littered with the corpses of soldiers, and there were still giant tombs in the areas of Puqi and Qizhou. Due to the great flood, many soldiers were submerged at the bottom of the rivers.

Not long after the remaining Japanese troops retreated to Nanjing, a mutiny broke out, with soldiers shooting officers and joining forces with the Red Army coming from Hangzhou, China. At this time, Japan was at war with the United States, and the people at home rebelled because of the hardships of life. Major cities such as Osaka and Nagoya fell into the hands of the Communist Party.

The breakdown of diplomatic relations between Japan and the United States was due to the United States supplying submarines, mines, and other military equipment to China, and Japan had repeatedly protested. Since Japanese transport ships were sunk at the head of the Bohai Bay, the feelings between the two countries became increasingly dangerous, and war became inevitable. (To be continued)

Two Brothers (8) (8)

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

"This is a Hublot (porthole)," Bill replied.

He pointed out the thick glass window that could withstand violent impacts and explained in detail how to close the porthole. This time Roland asked:

"Is the pharmacy also set up in your room?"

The doctor opened a cabinet, revealing compartments of glass bottles, each with a square white paper label on which was written the name of the medicine in Latin.

He took down a bottle and described the nature of the medicine contained therein, then the second bottle, then the third bottle. He simply gave a lecture on the method of treatment, and everyone seemed to be listening very attentively.

Roland shook his head and said:

"Is this very interesting!"

Someone gently knocked on the door.

"Please come in!" Wall called out.

Then Captain Boqiru appeared.

He extended his hand to shake hands and said:

"I came late because I didn't want to disturb you."

He also had to sit on the bed. Then the silence started again.

However, Captain Boqiru suddenly listened attentively. Through the cabin boards, he heard the order to prepare to set sail outside, and he reported:

"If we want to watch you leave the port on the 'Pearl' fishing boat and say goodbye to you at sea, then we should leave."

Roland took this matter very seriously. Undoubtedly, he wanted to attract the attention of the passengers on the "Lorraine." He quickly stood up and said:

"Then, goodbye, my child."

He hugged and kissed Bill, and he kissed Bill's cheeks. Then he opened the door.

Mother Roland did not move, with her eyes lowered, and her face was unusually pale.

Her husband took her arm and said:

"Okay, hurry up, we can't delay for a minute."

She stood up, walked a step towards her son, and stretched out her waxy white cheeks to him one by one. He did not say a word and kissed him once. Then he shook hands with Mrs. Lutsui and shook hands with his brother and asked:

"When will you hold the wedding?"

"It has not been fully decided yet. We will take advantage of the time when you turn back to Havre to hold it."

March Term Spot Gold Initially Weak, Then Recovers

On-floor Trading Depressed by Rise in U.S. Official Fixed Gold Price

Subsequent Vigorous Short Covering Leads to a Two-Dollar Rebound

The gold market was active yesterday for the March term spot trading, initially weak but later firm (hitting a low of $665.50). Including the forward premium, the final result was higher than the previous close. News that the U.S. government would fix the net gold price at $34.455 starting March 16 caused a temporary dip in on-floor trading. However, Western merchants engaged in short covering. Moreover, if the dollar's gold content is reduced by 40% (dividing 2.067 by 6, resulting in a 60% dollar composition), the pure gold price appropriately equals $34.455. Current buyers were then eager, as the forward premium favored bulls and reduced risk, resulting in a firm market. Initially, the overseas silver market saw increases in both London and New York. The Far East Exchange quoted future silver prices at only 1 to 7 cents, but exchange rates were significantly extended. Additionally, American cotton rose by 46 points, American wheat by 3.5 cents, and stocks by $4.53. Gross profit retreated to within $70, but sentiment remained positive, once rising to $71. A Reuters dispatch from Washington reported that President Roosevelt addressed Congress, proposing a monetary bill including the transfer of Federal Reserve gold reserves to the Treasury Department, the abolition of gold coins, a ban on all gold circulation, unlimited purchases of foreign gold, and the issuance of interest-free banknotes. These unfavorable telegraphic reports caused a drop to $65-66. Subsequently, the foreign exchange market tightened abruptly, and vigorous short covering led to a rise above $70. At noon, the market hovered within the $70 range. Later in the day, continued demand for U.S. currency settlements led to a tighter domestic market. Slightly more favorable news from abroad, coupled with active short covering by major players in the market, including speculators like Mr. Lu and Mr. Luo, ultimately resulted in a rebound. There are still many doubters in the market, so there are many unreliable bulls who are leaving the market. There is still an addition of shorts for speculation, but for the firm part, the shorts do not dare to short again, and the bulls are not willing to easily let go. Therefore, the market was found to be spiraling and extremely sluggish throughout the day. Each plate fluctuated by only one or two dimes, and the rises and falls were inconsistent. Trading also sharply decreased, with only a small number of rollover trades. The afternoon close was slightly firmer by one to four dimes. The trend is temporarily feared to have no large rises and falls. The final market price had more falls than rises, with a difference of only three or four dimes. The yarn market rose in the morning and fell in the afternoon. Although overseas cotton prices rose, and there was news of extended silver prices, it was still difficult to raise public confidence. The market's real demand remained calm. All regions had economic difficulties and weak purchasing power, so new buyers were very scarce. However, the rising cotton market made factories feel particularly difficult.

Food

Spot Flour Soars, Term Wheat Light and Firm

After the flour market opened in the morning, the market for each month saw a soaring trend. The quoted price of foreign wheat saw Chicago rise by $1.23 and Canada rise by around 60 to 70 cents. Moreover, due to reports that the U.S. President had a plan to raise prices, public sentiment was shaken after the opening price, and the price was invisibly increased. Also, due to major bullish players continuing to absorb near and distant terms, the market was particularly sharp. By the time the afternoon market opened, the sentiment for near and distant terms was further improved. This month rose by 1.925 cents, which was 3.5 cents higher than the previous day. Each month was also 1 cent better than the morning. Later, due to a small number of factories making a slight offer, and the selling price of Tianjin spot goods also being flat, with the battleship opening at 3 dimes for small goods and the gun carriage opening at 2 and a half dimes, public sentiment also turned mild. As a result, this month was 2.5 cents higher than the previous day, February was 1.75 cents higher, March/April was 1.5 cents higher, May was 1.75 cents higher, and June was 1.5 cents higher.

After the wheat market opened in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month had turned profitable. However, the transactions in each board were still extremely light. Partly due to the lack of chips and partly due to the decline in speculation, the market was slightly driven up by the high price of foreign wheat and the turning price of flour, but most of the transactions were still light. As a result, this month did not open, February was better by 5 cents, and March was better by 7 cents. The rest did not open. The current wheat was not opened because the standard had improved and the goods were sold by the customers.

(North Shanghai) There were 26-27 arrivals from various places. Although the weather was cloudy, there were still transactions for each good in the market. White glutinous rice, white yuan rice, and each pointed rice were similar to yesterday, and each had no honor or disgrace.

All Chinese ships were restored, and the previous deposits of the Fujian gang had been fully paid for. Yesterday, they continued to ask about the market. Other transactions were not concluded. Ningbo Gang also moved yesterday and handled 200 packs of Jiangxi machine late rice at prices ranging from 7 dollars and 5 cents to 6 dollars and 55 cents. 275 packs of Hunan machine oil were priced at prices ranging from 7 dollars and 5 cents to 6 dollars and 95 cents. The market prices were all 6-7 cents higher than the selling prices of the previous day. At the moment, the Fujian stomach is very greedy, and there are not many arrivals and deposits, so the future situation is still looking good.

Oil Market

White Tung Oil Declines in Hankou Market

｜Hongxiu Oil Opens in Shanghai｜

White tung oil rose last week due to the strong buying by foreign firms in Hankou, and the market price rose from 23 yuan to 25 yuan per dan. After this rise, the foreign firms withdrew again. Just as new goods from various producing areas were being sold vigorously, the arrival of goods in the Hankou market was naturally not small. Once the foreign firms slowed down, the market became depressed, and prices gradually declined. According to the Hankou telegram the day before yesterday, the price had fallen to 22 yuan and 7 jiao. The rise was rapid, and the decline was also sharp, and there is still a tendency to continue to fall. Judging from the situation, a drop to 12 yuan is likely in the near future. Zhejiang tung oil is also in peak production. In the past few days, based on the Hankou market, it was sold at 20 yuan, 3 jiao and 4 fen per dan, delivered in Hangjiang Qian. The fleeting boom has become a thing of the past, and now it has returned to 19 yuan, 3 jiao and 4 fen. The firms in this port jointly purchased nearly 10,000 dan this time. Now, due to the sluggish market, they have all stopped buying. However, the accumulated stock is already not weak. Xiuyou Wanxingyu, known for its top-quality products, opened 300 to 400 barrels the day before yesterday, priced at 29 yuan, 7 jiao and 8 fen. Dayouheng, Jifengheng, and Zhaoli all reduced their prices as usual. Hongjiang tung oil, Jiying, also opened at 22 yuan, about 1,000 barrels. Xiangtaifeng was reportedly secretly purchased by various firms and has been fully sold.

Hardware

Sales of New Lead Wire Are Booming

Recently, the Fujian and Zhejiang authorities have been purchasing new lead wire, so transactions are very prosperous. It is estimated that the quantity opened yesterday reached as many as five to six hundred dan. Most of the buyers are military personnel. The colors are mostly No. 8, No. 10, No. 12, No. 14, and other varieties. There are very few decorations in No. 16 to No. 25 and other colors. Because the end of the year is approaching, there is no news of price increases.

Pure Antimony Breaks Through the 300 Yuan Mark

Recently, there has been no major progress in the transaction of pure antimony, but the arrival of goods is abundant, and the inventory is rich, so people's hearts are unusually tired. Therefore, the market price has broken through the 300 yuan mark. It is estimated that each ton is sold for 298 yuan, which is another 2 yuan lower than before. Transactions involving printing houses and type foundries have slightly inquired, but other firms have not been involved.

Silk and Tea

European and American Silk Telegrams Do Not Turn

(New York's Current Silk Inventory Increases Significantly) The silk sales of various silk weaving factories in New York were sluggish last winter, the consumption of raw silk decreased significantly, and the year-end stock of silk was quite high. Since the beginning of the year, the import of Japanese silk has still been strong. Various silk and sock factories have controlled production and reduced work, resulting in a significant increase in the stock of current silk on the market. Yesterday morning, American silk merchants received a telegram from the New York silk market in early January. The total stock of raw silk in the city (as of January 10) reached 120,937 bales, of which Japanese silk accounted for slightly less than 110,000 bales, Chinese silk 5,039 bales, and silk from Italy, France, and other countries more than 5,000 bales.

(Silk Merchants Take Advantage of Low Prices to Purchase Factory Stock) The supply of raw silk in overseas markets exceeds demand, and the silk stock of various silk weaving factories is sufficient to meet demand, so there is no interest in purchasing more. European and American silk telegrams have not turned, and the sales of foreign firm silk are as sluggish as ever. Only the spring sales of inland silk doors have started. In view of the fact that the price of white factory stock has fallen to the lowest limit, silk merchants from Xun, Zhen, Shanghai, and other places have taken advantage of the low price to purchase 90 bales of grade B spot goods. French firms have also purchased 20 bales, which are said to be spot goods transactions, and the price is still weak.

Moroccan Tea Market Reports Decline

According to recent news from Morocco, the green tea market is currently exceptionally sluggish. The stock of Chinese Luzhuang, Tuzhuang, and Pingshui green tea is no less than 40,000 boxes, and Japanese tea also has 20,000 boxes. Due to the low-price competition of Japanese tea, the price of Zhenmei pearl tea in China has fallen by more than 30 francs per dan. Therefore, British and French tea merchants are adopting a cautious attitude towards the future of their business, resulting in Shanghai Tuzhuang old green tea being completely ignored.
