Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Talk

"Eunuch Tide"

— Li Qi

In 1934, on the eve of the war, genitals suddenly became important international "fetishes"! Initially, Mr. Hitler, in order to reduce crime among the small populace and for the sake of "superior races," forcibly eliminated the reproductive functions of many people in Germany. Soon after, for the sake of law enforcement, he subjected a German man who had raped a young girl to castration. Recently, in the state of Michigan in the United States, nearly a thousand boys and girls have had their reproductive functions eliminated. The fact that parents of these children were induced to sign consent forms has aroused widespread criticism. Whether it is the elimination of reproductive function, which does not hinder sexual desire, or the "root and branch" castration, it is always a partial or complete castration of the sexual organs. Therefore, I collectively call it the "Eunuch Tide."

There must be many who approve of the elimination of reproductive function from the perspective of "eugenics." At the same time, there must be quite a few who oppose the elimination of reproductive function based on the humanitarian view of "without descendants." However, I believe that whether one is for or against, one will grasp the core of the issue. Because the crux of the problem is not the pros and cons of castration, but the political magic of imperialism in decline, as reflected by this castration trend.

First, among the various imperialist countries, applying root-and-branch castration or partial elimination of reproductive function to people is nothing more than to punish crime and prevent criminals from spreading "bad seeds" and those suffering from serious diseases from breeding "inferior races." The inheritance of diseases and certain inferior traits is indeed a fact, but most of the general crime and serious diseases in today's society are due to the defects of the social system. The system of wage slavery and the "digging one's own grave" economic panic are constantly oppressing people to engage in prostitution or take risks. In other words, the current society is fundamentally a society that manufactures male thieves and female prostitutes, while syphilis and other infectious diseases have become byproducts of "urban civilization." Therefore, human crime or infection with serious diseases can always be bestowed by society, and most of it does not come from the "intimate relations" of their parents. Now, the likes of Hitler and American politicians and jurists deliberately obscure the fundamental crux of the socio-economic structure, specializing in preventing patients or "bad people"

from passing on their genes. This is clearly a case of "seeing a speck in autumn but not seeing a cartload of firewood," a feigned stupidity, a scam!

Second, the bourgeoisie initially avoids medical treatment for their own illnesses, but when the whole body rots and they can no longer hide it, they grab one or two superficial and insignificant sores, making a great show of "treating the illness" in order to deceive the oppressed in society, showing that the group of prime ministers and ministers are still somewhat capable. Hitler and American gentlemen have recently been using the method of eliminating reproductive function to prevent the spread of "diseased seeds" and "bad seeds," while encouraging the breeding of "good seeds." Their actual role in improving the national society is exactly the same as taking a sore, bathing and fasting, and applying a plaster, while the entire rotting syphilis is placed on the "slow lane." This is the fundamental characteristic of the bourgeois medical doctors; they will never prescribe a "fundamental cure" for the "national disease" because once they get involved in treating the root cause, they have to deny themselves first.

Third, now is the eve of world war, and the political giants of the great powers are limited to significant contradictions in thought and action. In order to manufacture a large number of strong cannon fodder, the imperialists are all encouraging reproduction by agreement. But at the same time, they also obscure the fundamental source of the anarchist state of production, thinking that the arrival of economic recession and war crisis is due to "overpopulation." Therefore, everyone imagines that stopping people in the lower and middle classes from passing on their genes can eliminate the scourge of war and lead to "peace." Therefore, the imperialists also want to eliminate the reproductive function of many adults and children. By observing the "Eunuch Tide" and the encouragement of marriage together, we can see that the imperialists, who are trapped in significant contradictions, have now gone from being embarrassed to "digging up what they buried"!

Exposing the magic lantern, the "Eunuch Tide" spreading in Europe and the United States is just one of the new illusions performed by imperialist politicians.

According to doctors at a hospital in Michigan, USA, many children have their reproductive functions eliminated because they have "strong sexual desires" and develop morbid conditions. From the perspective of "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for practical application," I would approve of applying this scientific surgery to Chinese warlords and bureaucrats, because if their sexual desires were not so strong, how could they marry so many concubines and choose even more young girls to devour?

Fleeing and Begging

"Preventing" Whose "Consumption"?

— Xue Fei

Recently, a so-called "Tuberculosis Prevention Association" has been initiated in Shanghai. They say that, based on a population of 100,000, 307 people in China die from tuberculosis each year, six times more than New Zealand, four times more than Egypt and the United States, three and a half times more than Germany, three times more than England, two and a half times more than Spain, twice as much as Italy, and one and a half times as much as France and Japan. Numerically speaking, this is a shocking tuberculosis mortality rate in China. Naturally, tuberculosis prevention is urgently needed in China at this time.

However, whose tuberculosis are we preventing? That is, which part of the Chinese population suffers from tuberculosis the most, and for which part of the population are we preventing tuberculosis? I want to raise this question first. This is a prerequisite question for tuberculosis prevention in China. If this question is not resolved, any tuberculosis prevention movement will probably end up with nothing.

We know that the sources of tuberculosis are: first, overwork; second, malnutrition; and third, unclean air. In particular, poor working conditions are most likely to cause tuberculosis in people with weak constitutions. Then, which part of the Chinese population is most likely to develop tuberculosis? Naturally, the overworked and impoverished common people, the malnourished and impoverished common people, and those who cannot breathe fresh air, especially the impoverished common people! This is especially true in large cities. As a result, the most likely people to develop tuberculosis are naturally the general impoverished common people. Since the general impoverished common people are the most likely to develop tuberculosis, then tuberculosis prevention should, of course, be aimed solely at the general impoverished common people. However, judging from past experience, this is not the case in reality. We often hear about so-and-so high-ranking official going to Mount Lu to recuperate, or so-and-so going to Mount Mogan to rest. And what about the general impoverished common people? Not to mention Mount Lu and Mount Mogan, which are like fairy mountains at sea, they have never even dreamed of them. Even ordinary hospitals charge one yuan for registration, and the most basic third-class ward costs 30 or 40 yuan per month, plus other special expenses, selling both men and women is not enough for half a year. May I ask how the general impoverished common people can prevent disease? How can they treat tuberculosis if they have it? As for the various sanitary facilities in the home and all the comfortable living conditions, these all require money. Especially in Shanghai, to breathe some fresh air, you have to pay to buy it. May I ask if the general impoverished common people can do this? Since tuberculosis prevention and treatment are impossible for the general impoverished common people, then who exactly are the gentlemen of the Tuberculosis Prevention Association preventing tuberculosis for?

The gentlemen of the Tuberculosis Prevention Association should not think that all that is needed for prevention is to formulate several hygiene rules according to academic theory and ask everyone to abide by them, or at most set up a few free tuberculosis hospitals, plus some tuberculosis prevention publicity, calling on everyone to pay attention, and that's it. This will not prevent the occurrence of any tuberculosis in China. No matter how much you talk about hygiene, no matter how many hospitals you set up, most people will be standing outside of hygiene, standing outside of hospitals, unable to receive your "real benefits." Only by thinking fundamentally for the general impoverished common people, who are the largest number of people in China most susceptible to tuberculosis, can tuberculosis prevention have some practical effect, otherwise, it may all be empty talk. However, what methods do the gentlemen in the Tuberculosis Prevention Conference have to think of?

Preventing tuberculosis, preventing whose tuberculosis? How to prevent it? I want to ask this earnestly one last time.

Page 19

Dogs and Chinese People Afterwards

— Yi Ping

Seeing foreign dogs sitting proudly in cars beside their foreign masters, licking their lips and smacking their tongues, I truly lack the courage to step into those so-called parks which, in reality, are private gardens.

It seems everyone acknowledges that Chinese people lack public morality. The foreign powers spent so much money and energy turning this wasteland-like Shanghai into the prosperous concessions we see today. Chinese people enjoy all the benefits of material civilization without any effort. Therefore, when they are mentally and physically exhausted and wish to restore their brainpower in the beautiful gardens, they don't want the uncivilized Chinese people interfering. It's already too foolish of them to work like oxen and horses for the benefit of the Chinese! Hence, the rule "Dogs and Chinese people not allowed" appeared. We Chinese people should perhaps forgive their good intentions.

However, foreigners ultimately prioritize harmony for business. Before long, we were also strutting in and out of these so-called parks which, in reality, are private gardens. Although it costs a dollar for admission, it is still the cheapest thing in the world. If you calculate 365 days a year, it's only slightly less than one copper coin a day, which is incomparable to our own Chinese-run entertainment venues like the Great World. After receiving such kindness, how should we Chinese people express our gratitude for their hospitality?

Furthermore, regarding "Dogs and Chinese people," I suspect it's just by chance that "dogs" are associated with "Chinese people." However, it's still somewhat embarrassing. If an ignorant foreigner who doesn't know the history of Shanghai comes to China for sightseeing, they might mistakenly believe that Chinese people are animals akin to dogs. Where does that leave us? Therefore, removing the rule "Dogs and Chinese people not allowed" would allow us to stroll around confidently after finishing work at foreign companies. It would also raise the status of the yellow race in the international arena. Personally, I don't want to sit idly all day, cooped up in my grand five-courtyard house in my hometown. That's why I came to Shanghai to live in a small "enjoyment" room.

That being said, it seems we Chinese are gradually becoming more assertive. However, our East Asian neighbor, which also occupies a place among the yellow races, is completely undermining our efforts. See the Reuters dispatch from Berlin on the 12th:

"Today, a German in a Düsseldorf restaurant insulted a Chinese man, calling him a heretic and a filthy Japanese, leading to a six-month prison sentence by the court. The Chinese man had pleaded for leniency for the defendant, but the court insisted on punishing him as a warning to others, so that Germans would treat foreigners with proper respect."

Although the dispatch specifies "Chinese," the insult includes calling him a filthy "Japanese," indicating a racial misunderstanding. Chinese people would not be insulted in this way. The rule "Dogs and Chinese people" has been abolished. Goethe came to China and found Chinese women "captivating for days." Therefore, Chinese men are not necessarily "heretics" or "filthy." Chinese people have long been fighting for respect. The most obvious evidence is that we can confidently stroll in the so-called parks which, in reality, are private gardens.

Furthermore, the passage "The Chinese man pleaded for leniency for the defendant" further proves that Chinese people are not "heretics" or "filthy." Chinese people are a peaceful people, always turning major issues into minor ones, and minor issues into nothing. The German mistakenly insulted another member of the yellow race. We are known for our tolerance and should "plead for leniency."

However, a dispatch is ultimately just a dispatch. If "a German" identified him as "Chinese" and called him a "heretic" and "filthy," then when I see foreign dogs sitting proudly in cars beside their foreign masters, licking their lips and smacking their tongues, I truly lack the courage to step into those so-called parks which, in reality, are private gardens.

Seeking my Shanghai collection of works, willing to pay with two volumes of the Lianhua Weekly. If any other payment is needed, please send a letter to V9, 3rd Road, care of me at the New Sound Radio Station. Sincerely, Yi Ping.

Where to Begin?

— Yu Gui

It's said that the first time one calls a girl from the "Quanyufang" in Fuzhouli, whose name hangs under an electric light (neon lights also apply), to a banquet or a high-class hotel, it's called "dǎ yàng" (打樣, "making a sample" or "tryout"), for the "táng chāi" (堂差, "escort"). An escort is just an escort, but to call it "making a sample" is like the hawker's chant when selling spiced beans: "Eat first (don't misunderstand), then pay."

Naturally, a girl with pockmarked skin and narrow eyes is not someone that spending patrons would be interested in. I often hear Shanghainese say that spending money must be satisfying. We don't need to give any more examples. Let's just talk about calling an escort. Generally, young masters -- I'll tentatively consider them young masters -- spend money to call a woman for entertainment, which naturally must be satisfying. Otherwise, wouldn't their virtuous wives at home object to their entertainment?

Therefore, escorts must first "make a sample." Thus, the girls shave off their eyebrows and put on fake ones, their faces are painted yellow (1934-style yellow rouge), their lips are blood red, they're not afraid of catching a cold in the freezing weather, always wearing a thin lined shirt, high-heeled leather shoes, and their bodies are all curves (imitating "body of love"). Dressed like this, they let discerning friends "make a sample."

For new movies being screened in theaters, as long as there is a sensual scene, advertising friends can use flowery language to write advertisements like soul-stirring, bone-melting, and many other death charms, and make zinc plates of inviting thighs that cost six and a half cents per square inch, then place them in a daily advertisement costing two hundred and forty dollars. That group of "making a sample" friends will naturally hold it up with both hands, as if it were their filial son.

Therefore, the full-page local supplements, the colorful advertisements on the walls, and the stale photos in front of the movie theater are all designed for satisfying friends.

Secondly, I want to talk about photography studios. They seem to be exclusively equipped for women. Occasionally, a lucky great man or the like can occupy a spot in front of the glass cabinet. We ordinary men are uniquely absent. Although this also grasps the key to satisfaction, it's even less effective than scratching an itch through boots.

There's a humorous joke: A humorist went to a photography studio that was being painted to take a photo. The staff replied:

"Sir, please come tomorrow."

"Are men not allowed to take photos today?"

"No, sir, we're opening tomorrow."

"Opening tomorrow? Where did all the women's photos come from?" The humorist pointed to the glass cabinet and said, "I thought men weren't allowed to take photos today."

Writing this, I still can't think of the most appropriate title. I really don't know where to begin?

Amateur Mailbox

Why is He Being Cold to Me?

Editor:

"I am one of the most avid readers of the Amateur Correspondence section, because it contains answers to many social problems and I have gained a lot of knowledge from it. I would like to start by expressing my gratitude to the editor." I now have a problem that I would like to ask you to help me solve. Let me explain it below:

Two years ago, I met a Mr. X, who had a very good appearance. Soon, romantic feelings developed and we often embraced and kissed, it was truly passionate.

When the January 28th Shanghai Incident occurred, my parents ordered me to take refuge in Hangzhou. We reluctantly separated and have been writing to each other ever since. After the Shanghai Incident ended, we returned to our original places. It was unspeakably loving when we met again after our separation. However, recently, I don't know why, he asked me to return his letters. I was still in the dream of love at the time and gave them back to him. Since then, he has gradually become cold to me. Sometimes when we meet, we just nod to each other and leave. My knowledge is very shallow and I simply don't understand why this is. I really won't understand unless you, sir, explain it to me. I am extremely grateful. Respectfully wishing you good health. Zhang Meichao."

Editor's note: Regarding the issue of love, people often write letters to ask about it, and we also discuss it publicly in the newspaper as much as possible, because this is the main source of trouble and depression for young people. According to our guess about the question asked in Ms. Zhang's letter, it is probably that the other party has found someone else, or that he is dissatisfied with you in some way, which has led to him gradually becoming cold. Outsiders cannot just guess about this kind of thing: the changes in love really have no fixed pattern, but it should not be without reason. However, it is hidden in a person's heart and unknown to outsiders. Since you used to be passionately in love with him, then you might as well honestly ask him "What is the reason?" This would be a more pleasant outcome. In short, love cannot be forced. Since a crack has occurred between you, it would be best if this crack can be repaired. If it cannot be, then I hope you don't delve into it any further.

Letter Received

To the esteemed editors: I recently read an article titled "The Election of Great Women" in the Talk section of your newspaper's local supplement, which mentioned that the Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) hosted the Women's Voice Magazine's election of great women, etc. This is clearly incorrect. The YWCA only publishes our magazine, the Women's Youth Monthly, and the Women's Voice Magazine is not hosted by the YWCA. The election of great women is even more of a misattribution. We are writing to request that your newspaper make a correction. We would be most grateful. Sincerely, the Women's Youth Monthly Press, January 15th.

Novel

Notes from Prison (10)(1)

— Wheel

"Allow me to explain my reasons, allow me to explain my reasons! I'm only referring to the fact that it's useless for the illness I have now. Sodium bicarbonate tablets are very useful medicine, and they do have a considerable effect on my stomach!" I didn't dare to say they were completely useless.

"But you clearly said they were ineffective!" He seemed to have released a burst of pent-up anger, changing his tone to a very peaceful one, saying, "You must understand that the prison treats you very well, very generously. Where else is there such a clean prison cell, such good food, daily exercise, and such good facilities in the clinic? It costs □□□ yuan every year, and the average medical expense for each prisoner is □ dollars per month. Where else is there such sufficiency? ... You say we should prepare effective medicines, and aren't all of these effective? To be honest, tiger bone and papaya wine isn't that expensive, and we could prepare it if we could, but we don't dare give it to you because we're afraid you'll get drunk and cause trouble. As for... the so-called improved prison is considered improved to the fullest extent. If you behave well and abide by the law, then we can report to the Ministry of Military Affairs and have you released or have your sentences reduced..."

His head shook as he spoke more and more passionately, as if he wasn't speaking to me alone, and indeed he wasn't speaking to me alone. His subordinates, the section staff and the head guard, were all watching. He could make a prisoner submit obediently after being beaten, and the prisoner would respond "yes" after every sentence he said. Now he saw clearly his position and his own intelligence and ability. He was now in a position of being a role model, and now he truly looked like a leader above all others. It seemed he was telling his subordinates that they should do as he did, that they should do so skillfully -- in case they encountered this in the future.

He couldn't overcome his joy at his own discovery, so he began to smile later on. He cast some triumphant glances at his subordinates.

"Yes, yes... but I'm very distressed that my illness has dragged on for so long without any progress. I'm very afraid for myself," I said.

"If you really want the wine, you can first ask the doctor, and we'll approve it after he approves it. You don't write a report like this!"

"Yes -- but I did get instructions and permission from the doctor to have my family buy it. After it was brought here, I asked the doctor to give it to me, but he said I had to write a report to you, Section Chief, for approval." I was trying hard to restrain myself, restraining all sharp words, because I had been oppressed several times, just because my attitude was too casual. Although I was stepping forward step by step at this time, taking the path of justice, I couldn't clearly state my reasons, and he wouldn't admit his mistake. Therefore, I used a tone of complaint to ask him. I couldn't give up the wine just like that!

"This wine is beneficial to me. I hope the Section Chief can release it! Can release it! Besides, many people have taken it before."

It took courage to raise the suppressed request again. It was very easy to be rejected in this situation.

"What you say makes some sense -- how do you expect us to openly give you this wine! Go, go, go! Go and abide by the law properly." These were his last words.

"Go back, go back!" The head guard Lin pulled my hand, because I was still standing there, wanting to ask for the wine to be released.

"I've learned something else!" I said to my fellow prisoners back in the cell.

Movie Special

The Film Artist's View of Freedom

— Ling He

If we pay attention to the trends in the film industry, we will not ignore the spirit of some film artists fighting for freedom.

First, we should mention the author of "Don Quixote," Pabst.

Since Hitler's iron fist seized control of Germany, and since Hugenberg, the boss of UFA, was promoted to finance minister of the Hitler government, the entire German society has been chaotic, and the German film industry has also become panicked and suspicious. Thus, Pabst was no longer allowed to create works similar to "The Coal Mine," and Pabst lost his creative freedom. At this time, all he could do was the lament of "The Threepenny Opera." However, the demon king Hitler still couldn't tolerate him and eventually drove him out of the country. Thus, in exile, he made "Don Quixote" in France. According to recent news, he has accepted a contract with Warner Bros. in the United States and will be producing "exposing films" in the United States.

Here, we can see that although he was forced to leave the German film industry, he finally left Germany resolutely and did not succumb to violent forces in order to obtain creative freedom.

In addition, we should also mention Marlene Dietrich, the protagonist of "The Blue Angel."

It is well known that Marlene is German. Because she is a world-famous actress, the Hitler government wanted to use her skills and treat her as a lovely "caged bird." At first, Hitler sent trusted representatives to give Dietrich many sweet words, promising her an incredibly high position. However, our Dietrich was not moved by this "honor." Later, a second delegation came. In addition to the above-mentioned methods, they also used violent threats. The representative said: "If you don't go back this time, you will never have the hope of returning. If you don't go back, the National Socialist Party will take retaliatory measures, harming you and your family..." However, Dietrich, as a great artist, did not succumb to the power.

Of course, there are many similar facts like this, but we don't need to give any more examples.

In the above facts, we can get a common basis, which is that they fought for freedom. Of course, no one wants to lose their freedom, and no one wants to be a plaything in the cage of the violent forever, especially every artist. When they cannot freely express their own will, they will be as depressed as they cannot breathe freely. Therefore, film artists must never be spokespersons for oppressors, just as they do not want to be parrots that can learn human language. This means that film artists should maintain their free will. We must insist on what we want to express in our works with the most resolute attitude.

Audience Opinions

My Review of "Auspicious Land"

— Guang Dou

For the sake of advertising appeal, I entered the Carlton Theater with 120,000 points of hope. The "Sold Out" sign hanging high at the ticket office downstairs further heightened my hope for this film.

But what was the result after watching it? Alas! Very disappointed! Under this disappointment, for the sake of protecting domestic films, we can't help but make an impolite critique.

Yes, in the impenetrable hinterland, the idea of ​​divine power and all kinds of superstitious concepts should be broken. "Auspicious Land" was produced in accordance with this meaning. Unfortunately, our director Shao competed in exaggeration and was unable to truthfully depict and correctly instruct, and even interspersed some unrelated things in it.

I grew up in the hinterland with the heaviest superstition, but I have never seen, or even heard of, a superstitionist who would spend a huge amount of money to seek an auspicious place. What's more, Xu Hongye in the film, dressed in a Western suit, looks like a modern young man. He would be so superstitious. Perhaps he is a Western-style superstitious person.

The long-time worshiper of money was actually complained by his wife a few times, and immediately changed his past behavior and handed over all the money he had gained through corruption. This transformation is so peculiar and rapid that it is inevitably too idealistic.

Also, about the matter of "chōng xǐ" (冲喜, warding off bad luck with marriage), I have only heard of men marrying a wife to ward off bad luck, but never of a father's illness being warded off by a son taking a concubine. This point is quite doubtful.

Linhua Village, which has never had a school, when a small school's establishment ceremony was held, some farmers actually sang the Party song, which really made me confused. (Omitted below)

Review of "Auspicious Land"

— Zhi Qin

China's film industry is really progressing like a rocket. This film, "Auspicious Land," can better grasp the future and herald a loud funeral bell for imported goods. (Omitted)

Here, let me describe a few points: (1) It very realistically depicts the irrational decline of a bourgeoisie, setting off the unreliability of superstition, as well as the one-sided phenomenon of the countryside, and pointing out the greatness of the interests of the masses. This is correct in terms of consciousness.

(2) The clarity of all the dialogues, as well as the clear recording of actions such as acting and striking matches and pouring wine, is the greatest success of all domestic sound films.

(3) The sword dance in the Farewell My Concubine scene, and the scenes where Xiang Gu says goodbye to A Liang when she secretly escapes on the night before Xu Hongye's marriage, the photography and lighting are well done.

(4) Chen Yumei has already given us a great impression in "Vitality" and "Struggle," and in this performance, she has enriched and magnified that impression.

(5) The novel insertion of three Peking operas, and Xiang Gu's temporary excuse to fetch water, as well as the fact that Xu Hongye, who was accompanying Mo Long into battle, suddenly got the news that Xiang Gu had escaped, which made Feng Jie anxiously look for someone to chase, were all unique clever points of the director.

Finally, let me write a few other thoughts:

(1) There are several whispers in the scenes. It would be best to speak louder so that the audience can easily understand what they are saying.

(2) Some of the dialogues are not very natural. For example, when Xiang Gu stared at A Liang as he left, her mother said, "Carry this load of melons back to the house," which is better than saying, "What are you looking at! Carry the melons back to the house," which fits the situation at the time.

(3) In the lectures and opera scenes, the recording is a bit shaky.

(4) The description says that "students and guests gathered together on the opening day of the rural elementary school," but there were no students on the screen, and there were no children's voices in the singing.

(5) The villagers, who couldn't stand properly, were able to sing the Party song "Three Principles! of the People!..." very neatly, which is a bit bizarre.

Lilian Harvey stars in "The Phoenix Seeks Its Mate," her only masterpiece since she went to the United States. It opens today at the New Light Theater.

My View of "Auspicious Land"

— Ren Wei

In "Auspicious Land," we can find three different themes: the first is to break superstitious ideas; the second is to criticize the bad habits of the old marriage system; and the third is to advocate rural water conservancy and education. With the above three points, there is no doubt that the content and consciousness of "Auspicious Land" are very rich and worth seeing.

The director clearly has significant progress here, and everywhere you can see his mastery of skills and many clever little places. For example, the insertion of three Peking operas is very appropriate. If played according to the old opera's format, these three plays would take at least three or four hours to perform; but the director was able to select the most exciting segments, such as Yu Ji's sword dance, Emperor Zhengde's teasing of Li Fengjie, etc.; although it is still a bit too long, (in my opinion, two operas are enough; Huai Du Guan seems to be able to be omitted,) but it doesn't feel very boring.

"Auspicious Land" is a sound film, so we should pay considerable attention to the pronunciation. Although the pronunciation here is not as clear and pleasant as that advertised by Tianyi, such achievements in the current domestic films are indeed worthy of praise.

The actor Tian Fang is a bit stilted; Zhang Zhenduo and Ma Dongwu performed very seriously, but there was nothing amazing; Chen Yumei and Ye Qiuxin performed very delicately and vividly. Ye Qiuxin didn't have many performance opportunities, almost only in the "Touring Dragon and Playing Phoenix" segment, like a昙花一现 (tán huā yī xiàn, ephemerals), but the impression she gave me was very good.

Sky One Jottings

— Rhino

After Wang Yuanlong joined Sky One, he starred in two films. One was "Youthful Hot Blood," directed by Tang Jie. The female lead was the model beauty Ye Qiuxin. The other was "Modern Lin Chong," directed by himself. The female lead, known for her robust grace, was Fan Xuepeng. "Youthful Hot Blood" is about to be released, and "Modern Lin Chong" is also nearing completion.

"A Female Star" has been in production for half a year. It has now been edited and will soon be sent to Beijing for review. The film depicts scenes from a sound film studio, making it quite realistic. Because Sky One specializes in producing sound films, the local scenery is naturally particularly lifelike.

"Fleeting Years," directed by Gao Lihen, starring Hu Shan, Ye Qiuxin, Yu Guang, and Lu Jianfen, is adapted from Zhang Henshui's novel. In the film, Hu Shan's scene of washing her feet and singing in the mountains and rivers is intended to be accompanied by a beautiful song. Gao Tianqi has already composed the song "Fleeting Years," but because the melody of the song is sad and not in harmony with the mood of the scene, Mr. Gao has decided to revise it.

"Fruit Shi Shi" is directed by and stars Wang Cilong. The female lead, Fruit Shi Shi, is played by Lu Lixia. Now, people in the company have made "Fruit Shi Shi" Lu Lixia's nickname, and when they see her, they all call her "Fruit Shi Shi."

Sky One has adopted three of Zhang Henshui's novels as film subjects. Besides "Fleeting Years," which has already been filmed, and "Peace Flowers," which is still being scripted, the script for "Happy Rivals" has been completed by director Qiu Baxiang. The main roles have also been decided, with Chen Yumei, Hu Shan, Yu Guang, and others taking on the roles, and filming will begin soon.

Since Xue Juexian and Tang Xueqing starred in "Platinum Dragon," they have not had any new works released. Recently, they will star in "A History of the Cantonese Opera Stage," directed by Shao Zuiweng. The story tells the love history of a Cantonese opera artist. The entire play uses Mandarin dialogue, which is quite different from "Platinum Dragon."

After Wen Yimin and Fan Xuepeng, husband and wife, joined Sky One, Fan Xuepeng's first starring film was "Modern Lin Chong." Wen Yimin's first film as a director is "Dancing Palace Spring Dream," starring Li Minghui and Li Ying, and it is currently being shot scene by scene and will soon be ready for filming.

Sky One will also adapt the world-famous "In Dream Lake" into a script, which is being co-written by Cao Xuesong and Tang Xiaodan. Hong Shen is also writing a script for "Metropolitan Scenery" in preparation for filming during the winter vacation. (Quick Reward)

Film Novel

The Cat and the Fiddle (8)

— Mo Chen

That afternoon, after everyone left, Dodd stayed behind alone. Taking this opportunity, he walked up to Shirley, took her hand, and said, "My dear, you know I've loved you for so long... and it's so sincere. Will you marry me?" "Yes," Shirley's voice seemed to come from another world, "Yes, I'm very willing to marry you." Surprisingly, the news spread quickly. One day, Victor was rehearsing the operetta when he heard the news. He felt as if the sky was falling around him. His success was already in sight, but it was too late to save the situation. Shirley, he had never forgotten her for a moment, but she had forgotten him! Shirley couldn't wait a few more days and was going to marry Dodd right away. His mouth was shut, and his teeth were clenched. He remembered Dodd's cunning, maneuvering him away to give himself a chance to get close. He knew he had been tricked by Dodd, but maybe it wasn't too late... If his operetta could succeed a few days earlier, perhaps he could still win the final victory.

Odette watched Victor with great interest. For months, she had developed a secret affection for Victor, hoping that one day he would fall in love with her. She often teased him with words, but he always remained cold and indifferent. She guessed that he hadn't forgotten Shirley. But now that Shirley was about to marry Dodd, perhaps she could find a way to make him change his mind. Later, she was alone in the dressing room, and she invited Victor in and openly declared her love for him. This made Victor panic and feel at a loss. Finally, he said, "I admire you very much, but I don't have any love for you." Odette's jumping heart couldn't help but feel restrained. She said, "What are you afraid of! Are you afraid of my husband? Darling, you don't have to be afraid of him. In any case, he won't know." Victor said, "But I don't love you. I love Shirley, and I will never forget her. Odette..."

Like a sentimental mood, she wrapped her arms around Victor's neck and said softly, "My poor, silly child, let me make you forget her. My darling, you make me love you to death."

The door slowly opened, and Victor was the first to see that the person who came in was none other than Odette's husband. He looked truly pitiful and heartbroken. Victor quickly explained, "We're rehearsing." Odette's husband glared at Odette and said, "I never agreed to you going back on stage. I should have forbidden you long ago." Odette rushed to her husband and wrapped her arms around his neck, saying, "But, I love, you're being too unreasonable." The old man said angrily, "Of course, it's mostly unreasonable for an old man and a young woman to be in love." Then he turned to look at Victor, and it was their first time meeting. He said resentfully, "You are very young. I am old. But I can't give up my wife easily. My only way is to not let her go on stage again." He then turned back to Odette and said, "Please decide for yourself. Do you still want to go on stage? Or do you want a husband like me?" (To be continued)
